Since I have completed for you, O Sons, this book, which is the final part of medical science with its completion, and have reached the end in it, through its explanations and clarifications, it seemed good to me to complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of practice, that is, surgery with the hand.
Since the practice with the hand has fallen into disuse in our region and during our time entirely: until perhaps its knowledge has perished, and its trace has been cut off: and nothing remained of it except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which have been altered by hands: and errors and hesitations occurred to them, until its intentions were closed, and its power was diminished: It seemed good to me to revive it with the organization of this Treatise according to the way of positioning, clarification, and abbreviation: and to come with forms of cautery tools and other instruments of work: which is made by the addition of clarifications and hastening what is necessary.
The reason why a good practitioner of this art with his hand is not found in our time is: because the art of medicine is long, and its author must be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, as Galen narrated, until he knows the benefits of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction, and separation, and has knowledge of bones, and nerves, and tendons, and their number, and their emergence, and of pulsating and quiet veins, and the places of their exit.
And because of this, Hippocrates said that the name is abundant with the name, but scarce with the work, and especially in the art of the hand.
We have indeed already spoken of this at the beginning of this book.
For he who is not knowledgeable about what we have said regarding anatomy will not be cleared of error, by which men are killed: just as I have seen many of those who are formed from this science and boast about it without knowledge and without experience.
This is because I saw a foolish doctor cut into a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck, and he cut some arteries in the neck: therefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead in his hands.
And I saw another doctor who attempted to extract a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large. He therefore came to him and extracted it along with a piece of the bladder. Therefore, the man died on the third day.
And I had indeed been called to extract it: and I saw that because of the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, he would die.
And I saw another doctor who received payment from one of the Dukes of our land for his medicine: and it happened that a black eunuch who was with him had a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the doctor hurried with his ignorance, and tightly bound the fracture over the wound with cushions and strong splints, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he treated him according to his own desires. Then he left him for several days and instructed him not to loosen the bandage: and he remained thus until his leg swelled with pus, and his foot as well, and it came to destruction.
I was summoned therefore to him: and I hurried to loosen the bandage: and tranquility followed, and he escaped from his pains.
However, the corruption was already confirmed in the member: and I could not restrain it.
Therefore, the corruption ceased to spread in the member until it perished.
And I saw another doctor who punctured the cancerous abscess: and it became ulcerated after days, until its maliciousness was magnified with its lord.
Which means that when the cancer is purely from melancholic humor, then it should not be approached with iron at all, unless it is in a limb that can tolerate being entirely cut off.
And for this, O sons, it is necessary for you to know that the procedure with the hand is divided into two parts: namely, the operation associated with safety, and the operation with which there is danger in most conditions.
And I have already alerted in every part of this book where the operation comes that involves fear and dread.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to beware of it and leave it alone: so that foolish people do not find a way to speak about it and dishonor it.
Take therefore the measure with care and protection, and attend to your patients with ease and firmness, and make use of the better way leading through God's grace to salvation and a praiseworthy succession: and leave behind terrible illnesses difficult to heal: and free yourselves from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation may not enter into you in your faith and comfort.
For it remains more to your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your statuses.
For Galenus has already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat bad illness: lest you be called bad doctors.
Now I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
First Chapter.
About the hot cauterization and the sharp medical cauterization, categorized and ordered from head to foot, with forms of instruments and cauterizing tools: and everything that is necessary for the procedure.
Second Chapter.
About cutting and piercing, bloodletting and inflation, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar things: and all categorized and ordered with forms of instruments.
Third Chapter.
About restoration, and displacement, and the treatment of twisting, and similar things: categorized and ordered from head to foot, with forms of instruments.
But before I recall the procedure with it, I must say what its benefits are and what harms it has: and in what temperament it is administered.
I say therefore that the discourse on the quality of the benefit of the cautery and its harm is a lengthy and subtle discussion, a science, and an hidden secret.
Also, many wise people have spoken about it and disagreed on it: and for me, a little of their discourse is sufficient, fearing lengthiness.
I say therefore that the cautery is beneficial universally to all temperaments, which are with matter and without matter: except for two temperaments, which are the hot temperament without matter, and the dry temperament without matter.
In the hot and dry temperament with matter, they disagreed. For some said that the cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the opposite of that, namely that the cautery is not appropriate for the disease caused by heat and dryness: because the nature of fire is heat: and it is inappropriate to be cured from a hot and dry illness with something hot and dry.
And he who says the opposite said that through the cautery there is benefit in every hot and dry disease that occurs in human bodies: because when you compare the body of a person and its moistures to the temperament of fire, you find the human body to be cold.
And indeed I say through his speech: because from experience it has already revealed that to me on several occasions.
However, it should not come to that unless one who has already been tested and trained in the chapter on the last exercise of cauterization, and known the diversity of human complexions, and the disposition of diseases in themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and the duration of them.
From the other complexions there is no fear for you: especially in cold and moist diseases. For all doctors have now agreed on them: and they have not disagreed about aiding with the cautery in them.
And know, sons, that from the secret of healing with cautery by fire, and its goodness over cautery with burning medicine is this: for fire is simple, whose action does not reach beyond the part that is cauterized: and it does not harm another connected member except with a slight injury.
The action of burning medicine reaches to that which extends from the members: and it may cause a disease difficult to heal in the member, and perhaps even cause death.
But fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not cause that, unless there is an excess.
Now this has become known to us through experience, because of the length of service and study with the art, and standing upon the truth of things: and because of this, I am excused for the length of my speech.
And if it were not, because it is not permitted to this my book, to bring you the hidden secret in fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies of its expulsion, by which it expels diseases demonstrated philosophically, which would be sharpened by your minds.
And know, sons, that they disagree on the time when it is appropriate to perform cauterization, and they place the better time in spring.
And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times: because the harm caused by the time is overshadowed by the benefit that is drawn with the cauterization. And especially if the cauterization is for pains from necessary, strong, urgent pains that do not tolerate delay: because it is feared that a greater mischief may occur than a small harm entering due to the time.
And do not let this fall into your minds, o sons, which is not feared except by the common people and foolish doctors, namely that there is not always a recurrence of that disease which is cured by cauterization: and they place the following consequence, but things are not as they think: because cauterization is only in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries up the humors which are the cause why pains occur.
Nevertheless, cauterization surpasses medicine by the speed of its health and the power of its operation, and the strength of its dominion: and it is possible for the disease to return at some time according to the complexion of the sick person, and the location of his disease, and its power: and what is prepared in his body from the aggregation of superfluities in him: and what comes to him in acquiring it from foods, and similar things from those causes, unless the disease is such that cauterization is administered.
A subtle illness in the limb of few excesses and moistures, like a tooth cauterization, because of pain, and similar to it, for it is possible that that pain does not return in it. But that happens in few cases.
But the common saying again, that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, is a true statement: not in what they intend by it themselves: for they believe that there is no cure which compares with medicine, nor with anything else after the failure of cauterization.
The matter is contrary to that, and the intent, that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, is not what it means, except that when we administer methods of cure in some illnesses, and those medicines do not help: then we apply cauterization at the end, and it helps: then it follows that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding of the common people and many foolish doctors.
The ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron: and they did not say this except because of the equality of gold and the nobility of its substance: and they said that the site of the cauterization does not produce pus. But that is not absolutely true: for I have already tested it and found that it does not do that in some bodies without other factors.
And cauterization with it is good and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you ignite cauterization with gold in fire, it is not clear to you when it is ignited according to the amount you want, because of the redness of the gold: and when it quickly cools down, and if you add more heat to it, it melts in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls from that into the task: and because of this, the cautery with iron is made faster and closer to us, from straightness to the operation.
And indeed I have already arranged this Chapter on Caustics according to the chapters: and I have ordered them from head to foot: so that it may help the seeker find what they want from it.
Chapter II.
This cauterization is effective for controlling the dominance of moisture and coldness over the brain: these two are causes of phlegm, and the excessive flow of fluids from the head to the regions of the eyes and ears, and an abundance of sleep, and tooth pain, and throat pain: and generally all illnesses that occur due to coldness, such as paralysis, phlegm, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar ailments.
The method of cauterization is that you should instruct the patient to purge first with a cleansing and dissolving medicine for three nights or four, according to what the strength of the patient, their age, and their habits require.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a novacula. Then have him sit between your hands squarely, so that he has already placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the tip of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger reaches, mark that place with ink.
Then cauterize with an oil fire: whose form is this.
Then place it on the marked spot with ink, by the descent by which your hand is gradually tightened, and you will turn it. Then quickly remove your hand, and look at the place.
If you see that the amount of alkil's head or the amount of zehrab is now exposed from the bone, then lift your hand. And if not, apply your hand with the iron itself, or with another one if it cools down: until the bones appear, which I have told you about.
Then take some salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cloth in it, and place it on the spot: and leave it for three days.
Then place on it a cloth soaked in butter, and leave it on the spot until the fire eschar is destroyed. Then treat it with the unguent tetrapharmacon until it is healed.
They have said that the longer the wound remains open, it expels pus: therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized until it reaches the bone: and the cautery should be held until something of the density of the bone is burned.
Then it is scraped after that which has been burned from the bone, then it should be treated.
And others say that it is necessary to use the cautery until it makes a deep impression on the bone so that the bone falls off, which becomes like the shape of a key: or an instrument that women place with a small amount of ink: and they believe that vapors from the head are exhaled from this location, and the wound should be left open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it is healed.
To me, these two types of cautery do not seem to apply to anyone except certain individuals according to a method of fear.
And to leave it, in my opinion, is better for its safety.
For the head is weakened by the breaking of its natural continuity: as we have testified in other members: and especially when the head of the weak patient is naturally weak: and indeed the first type of cautery is safer and better for me, and I use it: therefore act with it for safety.
Chapter III.
When chronic pain occurs throughout the entire head and persists in the patient, they use hellebore, cohimae, head purges, oils, and emplasters. And especially if it has already been cauterized with the cautery we mentioned and it has not brought any relief, then consider. For if the head of the sick person is strong in its natural constitution and is not weak, and finds intense cold: then cauterize with another cautery a little beneath it. Then cauterize the entire horn of his head with a cautery, so that it does not penetrate the skin, and uncover from the bone the amount we have mentioned. And cauterize it with one cautery on the back of his head, in the place which is called the vase: and it is the place where the suction cup is placed: and raise your hand in this manner, and do not uncover the bone. For the sick person finds because of that a very severe pain, different from the pain of all the other head cauterizations.
And I will say this is the Cautery in its place: and it must be a cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of the head more subtly than the cautery with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occur in part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and it is cleansed with purifying medicines for the head, and the rest of the treatment, which I have mentioned in the divisions of diseases, does not help: then cauterization is performed in two ways: either by cauterization with an acute burning medicine, or with iron.
The cautery with sharp and burning medicine is to take one garlic clove, and peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. Then cut the painful area with a wide lancet until you make an area under the skin where the tooth is caught.
Introduce it under the skin until it is hidden; then apply a moderate constriction with a poultice, and leave it for fifteen hours, then release it, and remove the garlic, and let the wound be for two or three days: afterwards place on it a cloth soaked in butter until pus forms at the site: then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do this with some burning medicines, which I have written about in the twelfth treatise, on burning mediines.
The cauterization of it with an iron is according to this method. The cautery with fire, which has this form.
And it is named Clauilis: because the shape of its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is something curved, and in the middle of it there is a small prominence.
Then place it on the area and hold your hand steady: and you should rotate the iron gradually with speed: and the amount that is burned should be according to the thickness of the skin, like its middle part. And lift your hand so that the artery below is not burned and bleeding does not occur.
Then soak the cloth in salt water, and place it on the area, and leave it for three days: then place the cloth with butter: afterwards treat with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this half of the head with the second knife end of the Cauterizer. And be careful not to cut the artery in this half of the head, not properly the old one.
On the method of cauterizing in the old half of the head.
When you treat half of the head, with what we have said from the previous treatment, and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and if the treatment does not help: and you see from the illness that what we have said about using the first cautery with medicine, or with fire cautery, is not enough for it, then you must heat the knife cautery until it whitens after you mark the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or almost that: and put down your hand once, and press it until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
However, you must be careful not to continue the cautery on the jaw that moves during chewing, so that the side or the nerve that moves it is not burned, which could cause spasms.
And be on guard and cautious about the flow of blood from the artery that has been cut. For there is fear in cutting it, especially for one who does not know what he is doing, and is not skilled or experienced: and he leaves the procedure right away.
And I will come with a reminder of the regimen of blood flow occurring from an artery according to its manner, and in its place in this book.
If you see from the illness that this cautery is not sufficient for it, and you see the body of the sick person tolerating the cautery on the top of the head as we have mentioned, treat the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer the cautery which we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with a cautery having two knives. For cautery is better than this and more beneficial.
Regarding the method of cauterizing for ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear due to cold and is treated with solutives and other treatments we have mentioned in the division, and if the pain does not disappear, then apply cautery with fire: and it is that which is called Punctum, whose form is this.
Then puncture around the entire ear with it after igniting it, as it circles around: or around both, if the pain is in both ears simultaneously. And keep the cautery away from the root of the ear for a moment after you have marked the places with ink: and let the quantity of the cautery be ten points on the entire ear, and about that.
Then treat the areas until they heal.
Regarding the method of cauterizing for torture.
Chapter VII.
The torture which is treated with cauterization is only of the kinds that occur from phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of diseases.
And avoid cauterization in the kind that occurs from dryness and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this kind of torture with plasters, and head purgations, and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the second a little below its temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cauterization on the opposite side of the affected area. Because softening does not occur unless in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of the cauterization is to cauterize directly at the upper ear extremity slightly below the horn of the head: and another one at the temple, whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until the amount of half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a type of knife, whose shape has been described previously: however, it is not as fine, as you see: and it must be a knife that is somewhat overly thick.
Then treat the areas with what precedes: until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in old apoplexy.
When apoplexy becomes old, and you treat it with what we have said, and your medication does not help, and the patient does not have fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on each horn of his head, and a cauterization in the middle of the head, as we have said, and a cauterization on the back of the head, according to what preceded: and the method of the cauterization should be according to what preceded.
It is also cauterized with a cautery on the mouth of the stomach: and it is the very last.
Then it should be treated with what preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in the drink given first to the patient there be hyraceum and pills that cleanse the brain.
Then shave the head of the patient entirely, and place on the back of his head a plaster of mustard as described in the chapter on plasters: and apply it several times.
This is indeed the method of cauterization: and do it according to the same order which I said there.
If therefore he is healed by that, it is good. If not: then make three cauteries on the back part of his head, which should descend from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye: and place between each cauterization the thickness of a finger.
Then treat the cautery with what preceded it.
If however you wish for an addition, and the patient is tolerant of it: then make a cautery on the middle. If you wish for an addition: then cauterize it over both horns.
Then treat it until it heals: let the cautery be oiled according to the form which was mentioned.
On the method of cauterizing in paralysis and softening.
Chapter Ten.
It is necessary that you proceed with the cleansing of the head with sulfur and with what we have said.
Then shave the head of the patient: afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery on every horn of the head, and with a cautery on the back of it, and with three on the cervical vertebrae.
If however you need more than those for the sickness and softening of the body, and the patient is tolerant, and the illness is strong: then cauterize it with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and the last with a cautery until it is burned deeply from the skin, and lift your hand. Then treat it until it heals: and thus oil the cautery.
On the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless his epilepsy is due to phlegm.
Therefore, you must first clean its brain with warm water, and with the rest of the treatment we mentioned in the division: when the patient is strong, or is tolerant in receiving medications.
If, however, it is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and cleansing mouthwash for the brain are administered, after many days with the improvement of food.
Then shave his head, then cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in the method: and with another cautery on the back of his head, and on all the horns of his head with cautery. If the patient is strong and is tolerant, then cauterize it with the cauteries I mentioned for those having paralysis, and softening of the body over the cervical vertebrae, and the dorsal vertebrae: and let it be an olive oil cautery according to the method that preceded.
If, however, the patient is a child, then apply a fine cautery according to this method.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize it with the cauteries we mentioned for those having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess inclined towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him in drink what will cleanse his brain, according to what preceded in the division: then shave the head of the patient, and make afterwards a properly made tortella from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and the patient sitting squarely shall be held on all sides.
Then apply the ointment. And it is more worthy from old sheep's butter. And heat it over the fire with moderate heating, to a degree that can be tolerated by the finger when inserted into it. Then evacuate it in the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools down.
Do this for the patient once every week, along with the rest of his good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small points, except where you hold the hand with the cautery: let it be smelled.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place on it a cloth soaked in butter, or in hen's fat.
On the method of cauterizing for water descending to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When it is made clear to you that the beginning of water in the eye is indicated by the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and purify the patient, with what cleanses his head.
And protect him from all moistures, and have him sit in a bath, on fasting for several days.
Then instruct him to shave his head, and cauterize it in the middle of his head. Then cauterize it over both temples with two cauteries, if the beginning of the descent of water is in both eyes at the same time: or from one side, if the beginning of the water is in one eye: and sever with the cautery all veins and arteries which are under the skin: and let the cauteries be as long as the width of the temples: and beware of the flow of blood.
If you see anything of it, then sever it immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with the wisdom which is in the extraction of arteries, and their severing, and caution against the flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, below two bones, with two fully extended cauteries.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in ancient tears.
When the tears of the eyes are ancient and persistent: and they are above the veins and arteries which are on the exterior part of the head, it is verified that this is from cold, phlegmatic humors: then cauterize with the same cautery as I described in the beginning of the descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries over both temples, and two cauteries on the neck below two bones. And if additional treatment is needed, then cauterize it on all sides of the eye cautiously, above the end of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
On the method of cauterizing for nasal odor.
When you treat it with what we mentioned in the division and the treatment does not help: then hurry and give the patient infirmocochias for three nights; then shave his head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with olive oil. Then cauterize it with a key cautery twice, above the eyebrows slightly under the hair.
And be careful of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the key cautery.
On the method of cauterizing for the softening of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid once with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it slightly above the eyebrows with two cauteries on each side: and they should be distant from both temples: and the length of each cautery should be according to the length of the eyebrow: and do not extend your hand with the cautery, but according to the amount that the third eyelid is burnt.
On the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs turn and pierce the eye.
Cauterization is done in two ways: either with fire; or with burning medicine.
In cauterization with fire, instruct the patient beforehand to remove his hair, if he is one of those who shave it, until it grows long and even. If they puncture him at their origin: then bind his eyes with linen, so that they do not move, until they heal.
When they have grown and are even, then place the patient's head in your lap: then mark above the eyelids of his eyes with encaustic, making a mark in the shape of a myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the mark be near the hair.
Then place a cloth soaked in egg white: or in psyllium mucilage over the eye.
Then cauterize with fire, the form of which is this.
Then cauterize over the figure you marked gradually in many places until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, appears properly burned entirely.
And the sign of the healing of your work is: if you see the eyelid already contracting, and the hairs rising around the eye puncture.
Therefore lift your hand then: and leave him for three days.
Then place a cloth with butter over it until the eschar is removed. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
If any of the hairs return after an hour, and the eyelid softens: then apply the cauterization to that area again, as you did at first.
If the hairs are on the lower part: then cauterize it until it rises to its natural position: and level it so that the hairs do not poke the eye.
It is that you should instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they lengthen and even out. Make a shape of a myrtle leaf from cloth paper.
Then take from known soap and from unslaked lime, an ounce of each or nearly so; then grind them together well, and make it quickly, so that it does not cool. Then spread it over the paper you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a cloth soaked in egg white: and let the patient's head be in your lap.
And place your index finger on the medicine and press it for a moment. And you should move it whenever the patient feels the sting of the medicine: for its sting is like fire.
Therefore, when this biting that he discovered persists, then release the medicine and move it with your finger. Therefore, when the biting ceases, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And then consider, if you see the eyelid rise, as it rises with contraction by fire or incision, it is good: and if not, then again apply medicine over the place where the medicine does not leave a mark and does not blacken, until your operation is equal and the eye contracts.
Then apply Cotum with butter on it until the burned skin is removed. Then treat it with diaphinicon ointment or another until it heals.
And it is necessary for you during the operation to guard carefully that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid becomes soft after some days and something from hairs struggles in the eye, then again apply medicine to the place that is softened from the eyelid itself, as you did at first. Then treat it until it heals.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of humans differ in size and smallness. Therefore, let your consideration be according to this: and the way of righteousness is not hidden from him who has a zeal for this art.
On the method of cauterizing in lacrimal fistula.
When you treat a fistula, and your treatment does not help as we have discussed in the divisions of diseases, then you must cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, and let the assistant hold his head between his hands in such a way that it does not move or shake with his head.
Then place a cloth soaked in egg white or in the mucilage of psyllium over his eye; then cauterize with fire using an instrument of this form.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's quill feather from one end, with which the cauterization is performed: and if you want it to penetrate to the other end, and if you want it to go up, try it thus.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then express the fistula if it is open, and extract the pus from it, and dry it: and if it is not open, then open it and extract its pus.
Then place the cauterization instrument on it, which is made very hot.
And hold your hand near the cauterization instrument by the eye, toward the nasal side, so that your hand does not waver or disturb the patient: and place the cauterization instrument on the eye fat, and destroy it.
If therefore you reach with the beginning of your cautery up to the bone, it will be well. And if not: then apply the cautery once, or twice, if you need that: and leave it for three days.
Then place the poultice with butter, and treat it with a drying ointment until it heals.
If forty days have passed and it has not healed: then apply a sharp corrosive medicine over it until the bone is exposed: and scrape it according to how it comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of the cautery for fistulas, which some first said. Attend to the location of the fistula and find it: then place a fine camahan into the fissure, that is, a fine cannula, whose form is this. And pour into it the quantity of a drachm of molten lead, and hold your hand with good retention of the cannula, and do not move the patient at all, so that the molten lead does not run or reach his eye.
And it is necessary to place on the patient's eye a poultice soaked in egg white or water.
For the lead burns the area of the fistula and heals it with a marvelous healing.
If the fistula is healed with what we have said about the cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the nasal passage and redirect the fistula to the course of the nose, according to how it will come to its own proper place.
Of the method of cauterizing in fissures of the lips.
Often fissures occur in the Lip, which are called Chaps, and especially in the lips of children.
Therefore, when you treat these fissures, with what we have mentioned in the division of diseases, and if the treatment does not help, then prepare a small knife-like cautery with fire, according to this form.
And its concavity should be according to the fineness of the knife.
Then place it, when heated, quickly on the fissures, until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with cerote until it heals.
Of the method of cauterizing in oral fistulas.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth: then it forms pus and bursts: afterwards it becomes chronic, and pus runs, and a fistula is formed: then you treat it, and if the treatment does not help, then you must heat a cautery according to its size so that it fits into the fistula. Then insert it, when heated, into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depth and end: do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards with what we have said about the treatment until it is healed.
If therefore the pus is removed and healed, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the corrupted bone according to what will come upon its head.
On the method of cauterizing in gums and softened teeth.
When the gum is softened due to moisture and the teeth are loose, and you care for it with medicines and it does not improve: then place the head of the patient in your lap.
Then with a fire cauterize it, whose form will come after this, so that you place a cannula on the tooth: and insert into it a burning cauterium quickly: and hold your hand for a moment until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
Then lift your hand: then repeat the cauterization several times, as you wish.
Then let the patient fill his mouth with salt water and hold it for one hour: and spit it out.
For the loose tooth is fortified, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
On the method of cauterizing for tooth pain.
When the pain of the tooth is due to cold, or there is cold in it, or a worm, and treatment with medicines does not help: then cauterization is applied in two ways: either cauterization with butter: or cauterization with fire.
The cautery of this is with butter, that you take cow's butter and boil it in an iron spoon, or in copper. Then take the cloth and wrap it over the end of the bandage. Then submerge it in boiled butter: and place it on the painful tooth quickly, and hold it until it cools: then repeat it several times, until the heat penetrates to the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool or cloth in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth: then place red-hot iron on it until the heat reaches the deep cavity of the tooth.
The cautery of this with fire is to apply a brass tube or an iron tube. And let there be something thick on the body of it so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
Then with fire cauterize it, whose form will come: and place it on that tooth: and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day or another day.
And it is necessary after the application of that cautery that the patient fill his mouth with good butter and hold it for one hour: then spit it out.
And this is the form of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever end you wish according to what is possible: and this is the form of the cannula.
Of the method of cauterizing in strophulus.
When strophulas are caused by phlegm and cold humidities, and are not obedient to digestion through medicines, and you wish for their rapid digestion: then use a concave cautery, whose form is this.
Having two open ends, so that smoke may exit at the cautery from the other end: and place it ignited upon the aposta once, and a second time if needed, until it reaches the depth of the aposta.
If the aposta is small: then place the cautery according to the size of the aposta.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it a cloth soaked in butter until what the fire burned is removed.
Then care for it with toothpaste until it heals in the shape of a tube.
Of the method of cauterizing in hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When humors bind the lung channel, and especially when it is with a cold disposition, then it is necessary that the patient be first evacuated with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it at the no crati at the root of the throat in a depressed area: and be careful not to reach with the cautery to the throat itself, nor on the skin, except slightly.
Then cauterize it with another cautery near the joint of the neck at its last vertebra ultimately: and let the cautery be according to the manner which preceded.
Then care for it with what preceded until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in diseases of the lungs and cough.
When cough and disease of the lungs are from cold humidities, and the patient does not have fever, nor consumption, and the disease is chronic: then cauterize it with two cauteries above the clavicle in depressed, gentle, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two nipples: and let the cautery be of a cannula according to the form which preceded.
And if you wish your cautery to be done by pricking with a cautery which is called Punctum, whose form preceded in the pricking of ear pain: and let the pricks be from thirty points up to about another.
Then care for it with what preceded until it heals.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. Therefore, it is alleviated with the cautery when you do three cauterizations with it at once.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the helper is displaced due to moisture and does not return at its usual time after being displaced until it becomes accustomed to returning, then it is displaced by a small movement as we have already testified, then you must first reduce the displacement. Then the patient should lie on their back or on the healthy side. Then lift the skin that is inside the Titillici upwards with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint is displaced inward.
Then take a cautery with two prongs. Whose form is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization will come with four cauteries.
And sometimes the cauterization is done with a cautery having three prongs, hence the figure of the cauterization then consists of six cauteries: and the prongs are according to the fineness of the wire.
And this is the form of the cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one is added to this manner, hence there are eight cauteries.
Then place ground onions with salt on the cautery. Then make the patient adhere to stillness, so that the limb is not moved for some time until it is strengthened.
And if the displacement is upward, and this rarely occurs, then cauterize it on the shoulder with a key-shaped cautery or with multiple punctures of cauteries.
For the joint is strengthened, and moisture is removed: and the sick person is healed.
On the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and excessive moisture occur in the stomach, causing it to be drawn away from its natural temperament and increasing phlegm in it, and usual methods of treatment are not beneficial: then the sick person should lie on their back, extend their legs, and stretch out their hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, a cautery under the spoon-shaped area of the chest the size of one finger with a key-shaped cautery, and two cauteries below from both sides of one cautery, until the shape of the cauteries forms a triangle. And space them apart so they do not join, when they would form pus.
And the depth of the cautery should be two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And the shape of the cauteries should be according to this form without addition: and if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery with which this cautery is made be one according to the shape of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by marking the area to be feared from this cautery: and it is, that you mark a point on the stomach according to the size you wish with an encaustic; then cauterize it with a puncture cautery; then treat it with the preceding treatment until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing the cold spleen.
When there occurs in the spleen pain from cold and moisture, or from thick wind, until it departs from its natural temperament by expelling excess, and the patient is treated with what we have said, and does not improve thereby: then the patient must lie down on his back, and you mark with encaustic three cauteries according to this figure, and this same quantity above the spleen below the hypochondria where the man's elbow reaches: and let the space between each cauterium be according to the thickness of a finger: and let the cauterium be straight according to the length of the body: and do not press your hand with the cautery too much.
And let the quantity that is burned be according to the thickness of the skin, half of its quantity not added: and let the patient stand on his feet.
If however he is not standing, then let him lie down, who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is possible for you to cauterize these cauteries with a knife cautery when you have subtlety and prudence in the art.
And beware that you do not proceed too far in cauterization, and burn the thickness of the entire skin, so that the whole body is burned, and it reaches the intestines: for the skin there is thin, therefore be aware of this.
On the method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
When it happens that one is about to depart, and you wish to know if the swelling is in the substance of the liver or in its membrane: then if it is in the substance of the liver, the patient suffers a dull pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the membrane of the liver, there is intense sharp pain with the pain; and you see now that its treatment has fatigued its physicians.
Therefore, the patient should lie down on his neck. Then mark the location of the abscess with cautery: then heat the cautery which resembles a rod. And this is its form. And cauterize with it once, until the skin is completely burned and reaches the siphac, until all the pus comes out: then treat it with the treatment for those about to depart, until it heals.
And one should not use this type of cautery unless their study in the art of medicine is prolonged: and through whose hands these ailments converge with experience on several occasions: then indeed they may dare to perform such an operation.
But to leave it alone is better in my opinion.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in pleurisy.
The ancients said, use a cautery with roots of aristolochia for cold pleurisy in the following manner. And it is that you take from the dried long roots of aristolochia one longer root, which is found among them, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then dip it in oil: and light it on fire. Then cauterize with one cautery where the fork joins the neck, and with two small cauteries under the slightly inclined parts towards the area below the beard.
And with two cauteries also where the fifth and sixth ribs slope towards the back slightly: and with another cautery on the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from the back: one where the two spatulas meet: and with two cauteries from the two sides of the chest, the lower cautery being between the two spatulas.
And you should not compress your hand with the cautery, but let the skin be clearly discerned by smelling.
And some ancients have said that there are those who use a cautery similar to a rod: and they heat it, and insert it between the ribs until they reach the abscess with it, and the pus comes out: as we have said regarding the abscess of the spleen.
But in this puncture with the cautery, there is a fear that either the patient dies immediately, or an ulcer forms at the site, which has no cure.
Regarding the Method of Cauterizing the Spleen Chapter XXXII.
When you treat spleen disease, and your treatment according to what we have said in the division of diseases does not help, then cautery is applied in three ways, all of which are correct.
One of them is to make three cauterizations, or four by lining according to the length of the spleen according to the figure of the liver's cauterizations, whose figure precedes.
And there should be the quantity of the thickness of a finger between each cauterization, or slightly more.
And the method of the cauterization, which we have mentioned for the cauterization of the liver, should be equal.
And do not compress your hand with the cautery: and let the patient lie supine on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: to ignite a cautery having two horns, which we have mentioned in the chapter on the dislocation of the shoulder: and raise the skin which is directly over the spleen, where the left elbow of the patient reaches: and let your raising be such that you lift the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauterizations fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert the two ignited horns strongly until you penetrate the skin from the other side: then extract the cautery: thus four cauterizations are made.
And if you wish, cauterize with another cautery having three horns.
Then care for the cautery after you have allowed it to discharge pus for many days: for it is more beneficial than all that has preceded in the treatment.
Regarding the method of cauterization in hydrops.
The cautery does not apply in hydrops unless properly positioned.
When you treat a person with dropsy using the methods of treatment we have mentioned in the division, and if the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize them with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery on the stomach, and another cautery on the spleen, and a cautery on the liver, and two cauteries on the back between the vertebrae, and one directly on the chest, and another directly on the stomach: and the depth of the cauterization should be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open so that it discharges pus over a long period of time.
And do not evacuate the weak patient after cautery with it: which requires that two intentions should be combined: and healing will hasten to him with God's help.
The shape of the cautery with which the stomach is cauterized should be claw-like: according to its previous form: and that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped: according to its previous form.
Regarding the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When abscesses form in a dropsical patient and are filled with yellow water: it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot at the knuckle, which is between the thumb and the little toe: and lift your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it: then raise your hand: and do not repeat it at all.
For yellow water will ooze out, and the cautery should be in this form.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the knife-like end of the cautery instrument: and let a cautery be made along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and another below it, about the middle of the leg: and on each hip two cauteries: and leave the open cautery without treatment for a long time: so that some water may sweat out of it: then treat it with the other things we have said.
On the method of cauterizing for the treatment of abdominal conditions.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
When there is a relaxation of the abdomen due to cold and moisture, which weakens the retentive and digestive powers that are in the stomach and intestines: and it is treated with methods of treatment, but it does not heal: and you see the patient tolerating an excess of power, then cauterize him with a large cautery on his stomach, as previously described for cauterizing the stomach with a circular cautery, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle key-shaped cautery: and a large cautery on the alcat (a type of gland) above the alhosos (a term possibly referring to lymph nodes or similar structures), or two cauteries.
And if you see an abundance of moisture and the patient tolerating it, then cauterize him with a cautery on the comb area, and a cautery on all the ilium: and perhaps you may add two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one.
For it is an effective treatment, whose benefit does not fail.
On the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the year, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupted moistures, and are treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment is not beneficial: then cauterize with three cauteries above the lower spine of the back below the almeidati briefly triangularly, and a cautery below the navel about two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is overly cooled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face swelling with pus, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery, as previously mentioned: and with a cautery on his liver, and another on his spleen, with a key-shaped cautery: and leave the cautery open for some time: then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you cut off althelul, then heat the cautery which resembles a rod. Then insert the heated cautery into the cut althelul: and hold it until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which the blood flows: do this once or twice.
If therefore there are many althelul, then cauterize each one with a cautery as we have described. Then treat them with what is beneficial for them from ointments until they heal.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery on an ulcer, it is worse for healing.
On the method of cauterizing an anal fistula.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
When the patient does not obey the incision and the procedure which we have described in its proper place, and is terrified by it, perhaps he may be cured with a cautery.
When therefore an anal fistula occurs in someone and becomes old, pus runs from it, and corrupted moistures. Therefore, it is more proper to examine it with a fine probe. Then determine the depth of it with a probe.
Then heat the cautery, which is like a rod. Then insert the heated cautery into the fistula itself to the extent that the probe entered.
And repeat the cautery on it until all the corrupted bodily parts are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the extent of your necessity.
And beware of burning the nerve, if it is there, or large veins: or if the fistula extends to the bladder or to the intestine, then be careful of all these areas.
And do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy area: and you think that it is not penetrating.
Then care for the area until it heals.
If however the place is sealed, and materials are cut off from it, and remains thus for a long time: then you know that it is now fully healed.
And if materials are not cut off from it, then you know that it is penetrating, or there is a corrupted wound in its depth, or something like that: of which the mention will come in its place.
On the method of cauterizing the kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys due to cold or severe wind, and it weakens the patient because of it, then you should cauterize over almethen on the kidneys, with a key-shaped cautery over the entire kidney, whose precedent has been mentioned.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time on the almeidatum. Therefore, three lined marks will come. Therefore, they will be more beneficial for healing.
On the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening due to cold and moisture occur in the bladder, until the patient cannot retain urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the scrotum over the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, and with one cautery on the right side of the scrotum and another on the left side. The length of each lateral cauterization should be according to the size of a thumb knot. Cauterize it with the lower back cautery or with two cauterizations if necessary, as previously mentioned, with a key-shaped cautery.
On the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and dampness occur in the womb, and because of this impregnation is prevented, and her menses are corrupted, and their onset is delayed, and pain occurs with their arrival, then it must be cauterized with three cautery points around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and a cautery above the lower back, or with two cauteries: and let the cautery be done with a key-shaped instrument.
On the method of cauterizing the anus in dislocation.
When mucous dampness flows to the socket of the anus, and becomes the cause of its departure from its place: and the sign of this is that one leg extends beyond the other when they are set side by side: and the site of dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore, you should cauterize the affected area above the socket of the anus with a similar circular cautery: after you mark it with ink around the socket, as it turns: and let the socket itself fall in the middle of the circle.
If this cautery is not available to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries using a large olive cautery: and the depth of the cautery should be according to the thickness of the skin.
Then care for it until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in sciatica.
When pain occurs in the hip joint, and its cause is cold and dampness: and the patient is treated with what we mentioned in the division, but the treatment does not help, and it becomes chronic: then it is necessary to rid the patient of thick humors with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and similar ones. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cauterization in this case is according to two methods: either cauterization with burning medicines, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is to cauterize above the hip joint itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make their depth good or bad. And let the space between each cautery be the width of a finger's thickness: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Sometimes, however, the cautery is made in the middle on top of the head of the hip itself. Therefore, there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form precedes in the cauterization of the dislocation of the hip, use one: so that the circle contains the entire hip.
And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of cautery for sciatica when the pain is attached to the hip itself, and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
If it extends to the thigh and leg, then apply two cauteries on the thigh, on the spot where the patient indicates there is pain, and with your cautery on the ankle four fingers towards the woodland side: and let the cautery be knife-like.
And the depth of the cautery should be according to the thickness of the skin.
If the patient indicates that the pain extends nearly to the toes of the foot, then apply the cautery where the patient indicates with a point cautery, three, or four, or more if it is needed.
And if he indicates the pain to be below the knee towards the thigh, then apply one knife-like cautery there.
And be careful in all your cautery work, so that you do not end up with the cautery burning a nerve or a large artery, thereby causing great harm or contraction to the patient.
And indeed, I have seen one or another of those who cauterized on the ankle and ended up damaging in the cautery, and the leg swelled until a tumor followed to the foot, and it was entirely perforated and corrupted: then there was an opening of the bowels, and death followed that.
If the pain is in both parts at the same time, cauterize each according to this method.
And certain wise men said regarding the cauterization of an anchor, for this is the method of such a cautery. Make a tube from iron, whose diameter is half a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a kernel of a finger, or slightly less: and within this tube be a third tube.
And let the space between each tube be the quantity of a thumb knot: and let the tubes be open on both sides: and their height should be about one knot or two knots: and make them a handle from iron suitably fitted to the tubes.
Then it is heated in fire until it turns red and throws out sparks: then it is placed on the anchor's lid of the sick person lying on their healthy side. Therefore, cauterize him with three round cauteries in one course.
Then leave it for three days. Then apply plasters with butter: and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Albucasis says, with this type of cautery, O sons, we have little used it because of the terror of its appearance: and furthermore, because we find few who can withstand it.
Nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries for those who endure and find their proper place with it.
The cautery with burning medicines is such that you make two jars having a perforated ring, into which descends the hinge of its lid made of bronze or iron, the length of the wall: at their height are two knobs, or like them.
And let the space between both quantities be the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above: and let them contain themselves together according to this form.
Then place it over the anchor's lid, with the patient lying on the healthy side. And press your hand heavily over the anchor's lid. Then pour between the two circles with hot water, which has been heated briefly with fire, and hold it for a period of one hour: and let the patient endure its stinging and its burning, for he finds the sting like fire, until the stinging subsides.
Then lift your hand with the instrument, and wash off the hot water from the entire anchor with fresh water: then leave it for three days.
And place butter on it until the blackness of the burning is removed: and leave it for several days, and pus will flow from it. For it is the final step in treatment.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg, make a similar treatment in the affected area as you did for the anchor equally.
And this is the method of hot water: and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and unslaked lime, one part of each; grind both, and place them in a new pot whose lower part has one small hole through which a finger can pass: and put another glass pot under the bottom of the pot: then pour over the alkali and lime sweet water enough to cover both by a finger's breadth: after this you compress them with your hand firmly: and leave the pot until the sharp water descends into the lower glass pot.
Then collect all that water and pour it over another lime: and distill until it is renewed.
For it will then be very strong in sharpness, which is used in many medical procedures, and in cautery of the other parts. For it effects the action of its fire.
And among the medicines are those with which the ankh is cauterized, even like tesiie, and mango paste, and lime with soap, so that each is well mixed.
And Galen narrated the treatment of an ancient man who was cured of the pain of the ankh and the sciatic nerve: and he praised it greatly. And he said that no other treatment was needed, and that he was cured with a single application, until he reported that he perhaps entered a bath carried in, and exited it already healed.
And it is taken from green seetaragi: and if green is not found, take dry, fresh: and grind much with some fat, and place on the ankle, where there is pain, or leg, or in the thigh: and bind, and leave for a quantity of three hours, or to the extent that the patient feels sedation from burning. Then put him into the bath.
When therefore his body becomes moist, put him into the seat. For the pain retreats, and it is healed.
And you should know that one should not use a cautery with these medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides said that goat dung, when it is used to cauterize the sciatic vein, helps it: and the cautery is made in this way. Let wool be taken, and soaked in old oil, and placed on the deep place which is between the big toe and the instep, and it is closer to the instep.
Then take dry goat dung, and ignite it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. Then repeat it. Therefore do not cease to do it until the sensation reaches the middle and the pain ceases.
And this method of cautery is called the Vaccinum cautery.
On the cauterization of back pain.
It sometimes happens that pain occurs in the back for many reasons, either from a fall, or from a blow, or from excessive evacuation, and similar causes, due to the infusion of cold and humid matter: and cauterization is only applicable to this particular type which results from the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after evacuating the sick person with foul pills and similar remedies, three lines should be made on the back where the pain is, according to the width of the spine itself. Once you mark with encaustro five cauterizations on each line, or more according to the amount that comes from the strength of the patient's tolerance: and the cauterization should be done with cautery points.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries using a median claw cautery according to this form.
On the method of cauterizing at the onset of hunchback.
This disease often occurs in small infants.
And the sign of the onset of this condition in children is that it occurs during breathing, lifting, and movement, and you will find at the last vertebrae of the back and its joints that it has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see this and wish to address it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is circular according to this form.
And let him take the cautery over all parts of the vertebra equally: and if you wish to cauterize around the vertebra with a cautery, make two lines or three: and let the points be near the joint.
Then treat the area until it heals with what we have said.
And beware, do not apply the cautery to the hump that occurs from nerve spasm.
On the method of cauterizing in gout and joint pains.
When joint pains are caused by cold humidities that are poured out into any part of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is customary for physicians to call this gout properly.
Therefore, when gout caused by cold is treated with methods of cure and the pains are not removed, then the cautery removes them.
And it is to be done that you cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the feet with many cauteries: and let the cautery be olive oil.
And if you need to make points on the surface of the foot, then do it with a pinpoint cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize it over the entire knee with three or four cauteries from all sides, using the same key-shaped cautery.
If however more are necessary to you by this cautery then cauterize it. And do not submerge your hand with the cautery, but let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
If however the pains ascend to the knees and the back: then apply what we have said about the cautery in its chapter.
If the pains are in the hands only, then prick around the joints, as two lines are drawn.
If however the pain remains in the fingers, then prick them, on every knot a pricking, and on the palm of the hand.
If however the pains ascend after days to the elbows or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from all sides.
And do not evacuate the patient from good regimen, from the reception of medicines. For if good is done by the regimen, and the phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with the help of God along with this cautery.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestine or hernia descends to the testicle, and this is an initial proximate occurrence: then it is necessary to advise the patient to abstain from food on his day. And let him use laxatives, so that the stool may descend from his stomach.
Then sit it between your hands on its back: and command it to hold its breath until it comes out, or the rectum or intestine appears.
Then replace it with your fingers, and mark with cautery under the rupture at the mouth of the crest, with a mark whose end is similar to half a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then with fire the cautery, whose form is this, until it comes white and throws out sparks. Then replace the intestine or rectum to its concavity. Then the assistant should place his hand on the area to prevent the intestine from coming out: and you have already opened between the patient's thighs, and placed a cushion under him, and another servant is above his thighs, and another on his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on the same mark, with your hand holding the cautery straight. And hold it until you reach the mouth with it: or repeat with it another time, if you have not reached the mouth with it on the first try.
And carefully observe the exit of the intestine during your cautery, lest you burn it, and thereby cause either death or great harm to the patient.
And know that when you do not reach the mouth with the cautery, your operation is of no benefit.
And it is necessary that the cautery for infants be fine, according to their size.
Then treat with the other ointments until it heals.
And let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you provide nourishment for the duration of his treatment, which soothes his stomach: so that the intestine does not come out during effort and evacuation.
Then when he wants to rise after forty days, then administer a properly made bandage, and let it stay for another forty days.
And he should be reduced from labor, and from fullness of food and drink, and from loud voices.
For when he follows this regimen, he is healed with a complete healing.
And I will speak of the treatment of ruptures with incision in its chapter.
When ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen and are initial, and you want to prevent them from worsening, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let what is burned from then on be like a third of it. Then treat it with what we have said: and it will not worsen.
And some have said first: that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, in this shape.
After it is marked with cauterization, and a line is placed across the width at the upper side of the rupture, and another line toward the lower side. And place your hand in the middle with the claw cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
On the method of cauterizing for pains due to falls or blows.
Chapter XLVIII.
When pain occurs in certain limbs due to a fall or blow, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medications does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize using the Point cautery.
And the cautery should be for the entire limb according to its size, and its sensitivity, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twist, and the pain from it.
If it is healed by the first cautery, it is well. If not: then repeat over the same cautery.
For it is customary for these pains to shift from one member to the adjacent one. Therefore, it is necessary to address them with cautery until the patient is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in leprosy.
However, lepers are sometimes greatly helped by cautery. And especially the type of leprosy that occurs due to the putrefaction of phlegm and melanchole: when you wish to cauterize it, consider.
If therefore leprosy is beginning to spread, and you have treated it with what we said in the division, and it does not descend nor remain still: and you fear for the patient that corruption may take hold of his entire complexion: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the known head, and the second below towards the forehead at the end of the hairline, and two above the two temples, and one behind above the cervical nuts.
And finally place your hand with the cautery for a moment until it makes a small impression on the mouth, and the scales fall off from it: so that the expulsion of gross vapors from it may be alleviated, and cauterize the spleen itself with the cautery as has been described.
If however the leprosy has already spread over the patient and is clearly visible: then it is necessary to cauterize with these cauteries which we said at the beginning, and a cautery on the end of the nose, and two cauteries on both jaws, and two cauteries on the cervical vertebrae, and six on the dorsal vertebrae, and one large one on the alhahosos near the tailbone and one above it, in the almeidati: and two on the hips: that is, one on each hip, and two on the knees: one on each knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the tender parts of his chest: and cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of his hands and feet: and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and on the palms of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, so as not to burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery over the mouth of the pelvis, and another over the mouth of the stomach, and another over the spleen.
And know that the more you apply the cautery, the greater the benefit and the more it contributes.
And know that the sick person does not find pain in the cautery as much as healthy people do: because their body is already numb.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of various sizes and smallness according to the limbs and joints: according to which precedes from the kinds of instruments.
Then care for the cautery with flour of the herb and honey, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in stupor.
When a limb is numb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and does not heal, then cauterize the numb limb with cauteries according to the size or smallness of the limb.
And let your cautery penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin. Then care for it with an ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes it is cauterized for a kind of numbness that affects the hand and foot at the vertebrae of the back near the exit of the nerves that move that limb: and the numbness is removed.
But let not one who is not wise in the anatomy of the members and the distribution of the moving nerves presume upon it.
Chapter LI.
When Albaras becomes old and no improvement is brought about by medical skills: then cauterize it with a deep cautery for a moment, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then treat it with the flour of the herb, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and blood of a dove, and blood of a swallow: let there be one part of each; mix all these together, and apply them on cloth, and keep in place until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in cancer.
When cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, as it revolves.
The wise have said that it should be cauterized with the final cautery in the middle.
But it does not seem right to me: for I fear that it may cause ulceration: and I have already seen this happen several times.
And it is better to cauterize around it with a circle, as we have said: or with multiple cauteries.
On the method of cauterizing in Adubelati.
When someone has an abscess and its maturation is delayed either due to excess causing it or due to the age of the patient being weak and having little blood, or due to time, and there is a need to hasten the maturation of the abscess, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by puncturing. Then leave it. For it will hasten with the maturation.
If you wish to perforate it with a cautery, then take a fire cautery, which has this form.
And place it in the middle of the abscess until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be from what follows for the patient, so that the course of pus may be relieved.
Then care for it until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in a corrosive disease.
Chapter LIV.
A corrosive is nothing but corruption in a limb that spreads and corrodes it: just as fire eats dry wood.
If you see a corrosive in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then use many cauteries, small and large probes, according to what is suitable for the place where the corrosive is.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you root out the entire corruption and nothing of it remains thoroughly.
Then leave it for three days, and apply ground sulfur with oil over the cauterized areas until all the eschars are removed, and all corruption is gone.
Then treat it with flesh-generating ointments.
If therefore you see that after three days flesh is born with a healthy growth, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not, then apply the cautery again to what remains of the corrupted areas.
And it is treated with sharp medicine when corroded. For it arises from the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is faster for healing: and I have already mentioned its cautery with sharp medicine in the division: therefore take it there when you need it.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in claws and warts.
Chapter LV.
This illness often occurs in the lower parts of the feet: and it is a thick, filtered substance that harms the foot.
And there are two methods of cautery for these: cautery with fire and cautery with hot water.
As for cautery with fire, make a concave cautery similar to the feather of a vulture: it should be made of iron according to the size that can contain the claw on all sides: and let it have fine edges.
Then place it ignited upon the nail. Then rotate the hand with the cautery around the nail until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail: and leave it for three days until it begins to discharge pus. Then apply plaisters to it with wild apples, crushed with salt: and leave the plaister on it during the night. For it will be uprooted from its roots.
Then treat the area with a flesh-generating ointment until it heals.
If they are not converted and often occur on the surface of the body, especially in hands and feet: then apply a cautery with warm water: and it is as you take a tube made of metal, or iron, or from an eagle's feather: and place it over the nail, or althelul. Then pour a small amount of warm water into the tube: hold your hand, and rotate it with the pressure of your hand for a moment, so that the edge of the tube is impressed on the root of the nail, and let the warm water find its way to the depth, to the root of the nail: and let the patient wait a while over the biting effect of the warm water for one hour.
Then leave it, for the nail is uprooted with its roots.
Do this one by one, until you have addressed all of them that are in the body.
Then treat them after they are uprooted with what generates flesh from ointments.
On the method of cauterizing in tremor.
When tremor occurs in someone due to cold in the nerve, or from quartan fever, or another cause: then it is necessary to cauterize with four or five cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and a cautery between each vertebra, and a cautery on his chest, and a cautery on his stomach.
For tremor is calmed with olive oil cautery, and recovery from cold disease is hastened.
On the method of cauterizing Albathir.
Chapter LVII.
Sometimes foul Albathir are expelled from the body, that is, pustules which are caused by corrupted thick matters.
Therefore, when they first appear, they should be cauterized on the entire head of the pustule with a fine cautery using myrtle wood, the end of which is ignited with fire. Or with the root of long Aristolochia. Or with a lentil-shaped cautery.
And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning of their expulsion according to this method: and they do not increase: and the excess causing them is dispersed, and they are healed from them.
However, it should be done after evacuation with bloodletting.
On the method of cauterizing in the flow of blood from an artery in a wound.
