Let it be made of silver or bronze: and insert the end with the nozzle into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the ulcer through the tube, until the ulcer is greatly obscured.
Then repeat on it many times until it dries up.
And beware, do not perform this treatment at the beginning of the onset of the abscess. For it usually adds to the abscess: and you should not do that unless at the inclination of its warmth.
If this instrument is not available to you, then take a cane, and attach at its end an oat husk: so that the patient's bone is not burned: because the oat husk prevents the heat from burning the bone: and this is a good treatment for healing with safety.
On the extraction of spines and bones from the throat.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
Often, a bone or fish spine or something else adheres to the throat.
Therefore, you must extract what is apparent from them where the sight falls, after pressing the tongue with an instrument at the base, and it is made clear to you what is in the throat.
And what is not apparent to you and is hidden in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach. For perhaps the attached object will be expelled by vomiting.
Or let the patient swallow a piece of celery, or a radish root, or swallow a piece of dry bread: or take a piece of soft dried sea sponge: and tie it to a string, then swallow it. When it reaches the place where the spines or bones are and is pulled out, then it exits.
Therefore, if it does not exit with what we have said, then use an instrument made of lead according to this form.
It should be thicker than the radius for a moment, and at its end there should be a curvature, which he may introduce into his throat with ease: and he should raise his head upwards.
And let him be careful of touching his epiglottis, so that coughing does not occur, and push the mouthpiece or the spine, or the physician himself introduces it with his hand.
But that the patient introduce it is better: for his knowledge of the location of the attached object: and push downwards, or pull his hand upwards with the instrument, the whole of it according to the quantity prepared for him, until it comes out.
On the removal of the leech.
Chapter Thirty-Nine.
When a leech is treated with what I said in the section on treatment with medicines and it does not help, then examine the throat of the patient in the sunlight, or near the sun after you press his tongue with the instrument that I described to you.
If therefore your sight falls upon the leech, remove it with a small hook, or with fine tweezers appropriately.
If it is not possible with them: then take a concave tube, and insert it into the patient's throat up to near the throat: then insert a heated iron into the concavity of the tube. Do this multiple times: and let the patient abstain from water for the whole day.
Then let him take a vessel full of cold water and open his mouth in it: and blow his mouth into it, and not swallow anything from it: and move the water with his hand every hour. For the leech immediately falls when it feels the water.
If it does not exit with what we have mentioned, then fumigate the patient with bugs, or with ash with the instrument I described for the fumigation of the uvula.
Do this many times, for it will fall.
And the method of operation in fumigation is to take a pot in which there are live coals with fire: and the pot should be covered with a cover, in the middle of which there is a hole: and the end of the instrument should be placed in that hole.
Then throw in the fumigation, and let the patient place his mouth at the end of the tube, and close his mouth so that the fumigation does not escape, until you know that the fumigation has reached the leech. For the leech will immediately fall.
If it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times.
And let the patient endure thirst, and eat salty foods, and garlic, and not drink water.
Therefore, it is necessary for it to be expelled with this regimen.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the leech is extracted from the throat when it falls on the tonsil.
It is similar to forceps, as you see: except that it has this curvature which is inserted into the throat. And its end is similar to the mouth of a bird which is named stork, in which there is the roughness of a file: when it grasps something, it does not release it at all.
On the opening of abscesses, and their incision, and general care.
Chapter Forty.
There are many kinds of abscesses, in various ways, according to the memory of them, namely one and another in this book: and they are different in piercing them and incising them in two ways.
One of which is a kind of abscess in itself and that which it encompasses from moisture.
And the second method is due to the locations in which it occurs in the body.
For an abscess occurring on the head is different from an abscess occurring on the anus: and an abscess occurring in a fleshy part is different from an abscess occurring in joints: and each of them has its own judgment based on treatment.
And among abscesses, there are those that should not be punctured until the pus is mature within them and complete: and among them are those that should be punctured while they are raw and do not mature according to completion.
Like abscesses that are near joints.
For when an abscess occurs near a joint and prolongs its existence until what is around it putrefies, the ligaments or nerves of that joint may be corrupted: hence it is a cause for the contraction of that member.
There is an abscess near the main member: for if you delay piercing it until it ripens, it will harm either that or through the main member.
It is near the anus, pierce it therefore while unripe: and it should not be pierced when the abscess is raw, not of complete digestion, unless it is near the anus, so that the deep part does not rot and extend to the interior of the anus, and a fistula is formed, or something incurable is formed at its end.
You should know the time for piercing an abscess that has ripened according to its completion: and this is at the subsiding of pain, recession of fever, and reduction of redness, and pulsation, and sharpness of the head of the abscess: and the other signs.
And you should make the same piercing in the lower part of the abscess and the more prominent elevation: and the piercing should go lengthwise along the body, if the abscesses are in parts of hands and feet, and in areas of tendons, and chords, and nerves, and arteries, and finally in all equal places where there is no reflection.
In those that reflect, proceed with the piercing according to that member.
When the abscess is in fleshy areas: then it is better to delay piercing it until its digestion is confirmed, as we have said according to its completion.
For if you pierce it before that, the course of the poison from it is prolonged, and there is much filth and foulness, and perhaps its lips and depth harden.
And some swellings are pierced according to the width of the body under necessity: or according to what the limb needs.
And it is necessary that you administer a small piercing in small swellings, and a large piercing in big swellings: or many incisions according to the size of the swelling.
And there are swellings in which it is necessary to hollow out the skin: and to incise when it has already become like cloth, and reached the point where it is already dead: such as that which occurs in many, like dubet, and buboes.
And there are some that are cut with a three-angled incision. And there is one that is incised in the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Like the swelling of the groin.
And there are some in which a round incision and a crescent-shaped incision are administered: and similar to them among the incisions.
But that which has no head, like mild superficial swellings, it is necessary to pierce it with a superficial piercing, or only flat.
And it is necessary that when the swelling is large and has already collected much pus, and you pierce it, you should not be hasty and extract all the pus at that hour: rather, extract a part of it. Then cleanse the swelling until the next day. Then extract some of the pus again.
Do this many times according to the progression, until it comes out: especially if the patient is weak in strength, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old decrepit person: for the animal spirit is often dissolved from the body with the discharge of pus: and perhaps the patient dies, and you do not notice.
Beware therefore this chapter with great caution.
And after your perforation with which you pierce the abscesses, it is necessary to clean the wound: and observe. If therefore the wound of the abscess is small, or the incision is flat, then apply lint from linen, or old felt. And if the abscess is large, and there are many perforation fissures, then you must insert lint into each fissure until they reach the joint.
And if you have cut part of the skin in the abscess, or scraped it around: then you must fill it with old felt, or as when a cloth is woven, or combed with flax down without moisture: and bind it until the third day.
Then remove it, and treat it with the appropriate ointment until it heals.
If however a flow of blood occurs during your operation, then apply cold water and vinegar, after the cloth has been soaked in them: and place it on the site of the bleeding multiple times.
If however the flow of blood persists, then you must administer treatment, and cure, and powders, which I have described in many places in this book, and in divisions.
If however it is in winter time, and the place of the abscess is of many nerves: then it is necessary that you pour finely ground [substances] with warm wine, and oil: and place them upon the area.
And if it is in summer, and the areas are fleshy: then it is necessary that you place finely ground [substances] soaked in water and oil, or with wine and oil, and all of that cold. Until when it will be the third day, as we said, then it is necessary that you open the abscess, and clean it, and administer to its cure what is appropriate for it, until it heals.
This therefore is what is necessary from the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses universally.
According to the path of distinction, I have already spoken about every abscess, how the way to its cure is specified individually.
Chapter XLI.
Regarding the incision of abscesses that occur on the scalp.
Small abscesses occur on the scalp, and they are of the kinds of Knots, which are contained in the layers that serve as their sacks: almost like they are the egg follicles of a hen.
And their kinds are many.
Some of them are fatty: and some contain moisture similar to mud: and some contain moisture similar to boiled grains and porridges: and others similar to these, and some are hard like stone.
And in the cutting of all and their extraction there is no fear, as long as at their cutting the artery does not make opposition.
And the operation in cutting them is to examine them with an instrument whose form comes after this, which is named Intromissum, until you know what it contains.
For if it contains moisture, then cut it with a longitudinal superficial cut: in this manner.
And begin with a cut from line b to line g. When the moisture is evacuated, then scrape the cyst that contains the moisture, and do not leave anything of it entirely.
For it often returns if any part of it remains.
Then soak the cloth in Egyptian ointment, if it is available: and if not, in water and salt: and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day. For what remains from the cyst will be corroded.
Then repeat over the cloth with the Egyptian ointment a second and third time, and if necessary do so until you are confident that nothing of the cyst remains, then treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
If the aposteme contains a fatty knot: then cut it in this manner, with a cross-shaped incision: and insert hooks between the two lips of the incision, and scrape it from all sides: and endeavor to extract the tissue that contains it.
If however the artery opposes you, then do what I will tell you next.
And similarly do for an abscess, if it is stony, by incision, and the same treatment, according to what we have said.
And incision on a stony abscess is easier: because it has little blood and moisture. And sometimes there are some of these abscesses that are on the head in some individuals, which completely lack moisture.
Which means: I incised an abscess on the head of an old woman, and I found the abscess like a solid, hard, rough, white stone that could not be broken: and if struck with it, it would wound someone.
In other abscesses occurring on the head, besides these abscesses which occur on the heads of children and near the roots of the ears, the incision of all of them should be superficial.
Or make the puncture always from the lower part of them, so that the flow of pus is directed downwards.
Then treat it with what is appropriate for them from the treatment.
Regarding the incision of strophulas on the neck.
Chapter XLII.
These abscesses often occur on the neck, under the jawbones, and in the groin: and sometimes they occur on the rest of the body.
And regarding those that occur on the neck, there is one and many: and they are generated from each other: and every Strophula among them is within its own coat, as it is with knots and abscesses of the head, as we have narrated.
And there are many kinds of these Strophulas. And among them are stone-like ones: and among them are those that contain humors: and among them are malignant ones, which do not obey treatment.
In that one which you see of good disposition to the touch, whose color is clearly near to the skin's color, and moves to every part, and is not attached with the neck nerves, nor with glands, nor with arteries, nor is it deep: it is necessary to cut it with a superficial incision from the upper part to the lower part of the body along line b. to line g., and peel it away from all sides: and stretch the two skin lips with a hook, or with many hooks if you need them, as we said in abscesses of the head, and extract it gradually.
And be cautious so that neither vein nor nerve is cut.
And let the scalpel not be very sharp: so that it does not make your hand shake during the incision, or disturb the patient, and cut what is not necessary.
If you do cut a vein or artery, or if it prevents you from continuing the operation, then apply ground zegi or certain powders that stop the flow of blood to the wound, and bind the wound, and leave it until the sharpness of the abscess has subsided and the wound has softened: or it begins to turn and tend toward putrefaction.
For the blood is congealed by the lint. Return therefore to your operation until you complete it.
Then inquire with your index finger if anything of the small Strophulus remains; therefore cut them and clean them.
If there is a large vein at the root of the Strophula, then you must not cut that Strophula from its root; rather, you must tie it with a strong double thread and leave it until it falls off by itself without harm.
Then fill the wound with old wool that you have already soaked in Egyptian ointment. Then care for it.
If the Strophula is cut entirely, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound: and sew it up immediately, as soon as you see that there is absolutely no excess remaining.
If you see that there is excess remaining due to the size of the Strophula, then you must proceed to cut its root and remove it: and apply the suture as we have said.
And for those Strophulas that contain moistures, pierce them with a superficial puncture so that the site of their maturity is apparent to you: and place the puncture from what follows below the body, as we have said.
Then apply licinia with ointment after the puncture, and similar treatments, to corrode what remains of the corruption, until you see the wound already cleansed: then treat it with flesh-generating ointment until it heals.
Chapter XLIII.
On the incision of the epiglottis when an abscess occurs within the throat.
The ancients said this incision on the epiglottis, and I have not seen anyone in our land who has done it: and this is the writing of their speech.
In those having a synanche, however, it is necessary that the incision of the epiglottis be avoided: since no benefit is achieved through it: therefore, because all the veins and lung are weakened.
In those who have a warm abscess in the mouth, or throat, or both tonsils, when there is no illness in the canal, it is necessary to use the incision of the epiglottis, to avoid the danger that arises from obstruction.
Therefore, when we wish to do this, we should cut the epiglottis below three or four circles of the epiglottis, with a small incision in width, in what is between two circles by the amount that the incision is on the surface, not in the cartilage: and this place is suitable for the incision because it is devoid of flesh, and the blood vessels are far from it.
If the surgeon is timid, then he must stretch the skin of the throat with a hook. Then he should incise the skin until he reaches the canal: avoid the blood vessel, if he sees any of them.
Then he should cut the surface that we have mentioned: and it is indicated over the incision of the canal by the phlegm that comes out of it, along with what is disrupted, and by the cutting of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
And when the time feared for suffocation has passed, bring together the two lips of the skin wound, and sew only the skin itself without the cartilage.
Then apply medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Albucasis says. The summary of this discourse we have narrated is not explained unless they see that some of these abscesses have already swollen the patient's throat: and the patient has risen above death, and wishes to cut off his breathing: they go to cut the epiglottis so that the patient may breathe over the wound place with a certain respiration and be saved from death: and for this reason they commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is consumed, and it lasts for three days or nearly so: then they command to sew the wound and treat it until it is healed.
And what I saw with my own eyes is that a certain servant took a knife and inserted it into her throat, and cut a part of the windpipe.
And I was called for her treatment, and I found her gasping, as one who is near death.
I uncovered the wound and found a small amount of blood that had come out of it. Therefore, I was confident that she had not cut the vein or the windpipe: and air was escaping from the wound.
I hastened therefore, and treated his wound, and cured it until it was healed: and nothing happened to the servant except hoarseness in her voice: and she returned after days to a better state of health.
Therefore, I say that there is no fear in the incision of the epiglottis.
Regarding the incision of the throat hernia.
Chapter XLIV.
This swelling named throat hernia is a large swelling according to the color of the body: and it is very common in women.
And it occurs in two ways: either it is natural, or it is accidental.
In the natural case, there is certainly no malice.
The accidental, however, occurs in two ways: one of which is similar to fatty knots. And the other way is similar to the swelling that occurs from the knotting of an artery. And there is fear in it, and one should not presumptuously approach it with iron, unless it is small: and you should examine it and investigate it with an introducer. If you find it similar to a fatty knot and it is not suspended with any veins, then cut it as knots are cut: and extract it along with what it contains from the cyst, if it is in a cyst: and if not, then thoroughly examine the entire area. Then treat the area with what is necessary for the healing until it is healed.
Chapter Forty-Five.
On the incision concerning the types of Nodes.
There are many types of nodes, and I have already mentioned all their types in the division: and it is necessary that I describe here the difference between a node and an excrescence, as it causes confusion.
I say therefore, that when an excrescence is accompanied by heat, fever, and severe pains, until the effervescence of the superfluity is calmed and putrefaction is complete, then the fever and heat subside.
With a node, there is no heat, no fever, no pains, and they are contained in cysts called sifachin, which are their own sacs, and they are according to the color of the body: and their beginning is like a chickpea, and they become like a batecha, and may be larger or smaller.
And they are of two types: either fatty, or containing humidity. And the colors of the humidity are many, according to what I have said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the treatment of a node, you must examine it and inquire about it first with an instrument called Intromissum, according to how its form will be presented in the chapter that follows this.
And the method of examining swellings and all nodes is to take this instrument and insert it into the moister place you find in the swelling: and you should gradually rotate your fingers with it until you know that the instrument has penetrated the skin. Then place your hand at the measure of the size of the abscess.
Then remove the inserted object, and examine what comes out after it.
If then a flowing moisture comes out, whatever the color may be: then cut it with a superficial incision, as I have said in the other abscesses.
And if no moisture comes out after the inserted object, then you know that it is thick: therefore cut over it with a cross-shaped incision, in this form, as I have taught you: and suspend it with hooks, and remove the skin from all sides easily: and apply the cupping vessel if you can over it, to extract the healthy tissue with the knot.
If, however, the cupping vessel breaks during the operation, and it is not possible to extract the healthy tissue, for this often happens, then remove it in pieces until nothing remains of it.
For if any part of it remains, whether little or much, the knot returns in full measure.
If it overcomes you and a little of it remains: then fill the wound at your completion with some sharp corrosive powders: bind the wound, and place something warm over it where the abscess sits, and care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
If then the knot is large, then suture its two lips, and care for it with what promotes fleshing.
If, however, there is a pulsating or non-pulsating vein against you: then hurry and fill the place with ground zegi, and leave it tight for two or three days until the wound becomes putrefied and the blood boiling ceases: then return to incising what remains of the knot.
Chapter Forty-Six.
On the instruments for cutting and piercing.
There are forms of speculums, and they are of three kinds.
Among them is the large one, and among them is the medium one, and among them is the small one.
Let them be made of square-ended alfulud iron appropriately, so that they may quickly enter into the abscess.
And these are the forms of perforating instruments, and one of them is called beris, that is, perforator: and they are of three kinds.
Among them is the large one, and the medium one, and the small one.
They are used to investigate abscesses, sinuses, fistulas, and buboes from what is between them of bones.
And others are made round, smooth, and blunt, like large needles with which chairs are sewn, made of brass, or copper, or iron, or silver.
And the better ones are those made of brass.
And perforating instruments are also made of black lead, which are used to examine fistulas, whose concavity has reflections, so that they can be gently reflected with those reflections.
And they are again of three kinds. For among them are the long ones, the medium ones, and the short ones, according to the size of the width of the fistula and its narrowness.
The form of forceps, and they are of many kinds.
For they are simple, that is, they have one curvature: and they are of three kinds as you see, Great, Medium, and Small.
And among them are blind forceps: and they are of three kinds.
And among them are hooks having two curvatures, and they are of three kinds: and among them are hooks having three curvatures, and they are of three kinds: and all these are necessary in their place.
And these are the forms of scalpels, with which knots and abscesses are cut and skinned: and they are of three kinds: for among them there is a large, medium, and small one.
Their ends with which the cutting is done are sharp, other ends are not sharp: and they are not used thus, except to aid in skimming knots near a fear of vein or nerve incision: and to heal through them the sick and find temporary relief from burning, which is found in skimming abscesses.
They are made of bronze and resemble a still with which alcohol is made: and at the wide end there are hidden points of spatula: and it runs to the interior and the exterior when you wish, as you see.
The form of spatulas which are hidden between the fingers during the piercing of abscesses: and the sick do not feel them: and they are of three kinds, large, medium, and small.
Forms of Venous Arteries with which the flow of blood is cut off: and they are of three species, large, medium, and small.
Let them be made of bronze or citrus wood, round, to a moderate length, as you see: and let them be fine.
And it is necessary for those species of veins to be with you, large and small: so that you may cut off the blood quickly in an emergency, and then when medicine is not present for you.
However, do not use them to cut off the blood flow in every part of the body, and use them only in fleshy areas: such as the calves of the legs, the hips, the arms, the nipples, the abdomen, the groin, and similar fleshy, moist areas.
And sometimes small instruments similar to the rinds of onions are made from them according to their shape: with which the blood is cut off when it flows from the place of bloodletting, or at the incision of a vein, or artery: and sometimes they are made round according to this form.
Chapter XLVII.
Regarding the treatment of men's nipples which resemble women's nipples.
Sometimes the nipples of some men swell during the completion of sleep (that is, when they begin to emit semen in sleep) until they resemble women's nipples: and they remain foully abscessed.
Therefore, for those who wish to avoid this, it is necessary to cut above the nipples with a crescent-shaped incision, according to this form from line b to line g. Then remove all the fat. Then fill the wound with a flesh-forming medicine. Then bring together the two lips of the wound with a suture, and care for it until it heals.
If the nipple inclines downwards and softens due to its size, as often happens with women: then it must be incised on its two upper sides with two similar crescent-shaped cuts, each of which is connected to the other at the ends of both, until a larger line contains a smaller one, according to this form from line b to line g. Then remove the skin that is between the two lips and take away the fat, and administer what we have said about suturing and powders, which is necessary for the cure, until it heals.
If you cannot complete the incision that you are supposed to make due to the patient's restlessness or due to blood flow: then you must fill the wound with a linen dipped in a corrosive ointment, and leave it until it corrodes what remains of the fat. Then care for it until it heals.
Regarding the puncturing of an abscess, which occurs under the Titillico.
Chapter XLVIII.
These abscesses which occur under the Titillico are of the hard species of Strophularia, which contains cysts, and among them are those which contain moisture.
Those among them which contain moisture should be incised with a crescent-shaped cut, according to this form, from line b to line g. When all the pus in the abscess has been evacuated, then fill it with an old cloth and leave it until the next day.
Then the scab shall be removed, and it should be treated with a suitable ointment until it heals.
If the abscess is of the kind of knots like Strophularia, then cut above it, as we have said in the section on cutting equally above Strophularia.
If the wound extends so as to discharge pus, then apply a cautery to it, according to what we have said in the preceding.
Chapter XLIX.
Regarding the incision of an abscess that occurs due to the artery and vein.
When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it becomes hardened, an abscess often results from this: and similarly with veins, so that an abscess and swelling occur in them.
And the signs by which it is known that the abscess and swelling are due to the artery and vein are: for when the abscess is due to the artery, it is long, gathered deep in the body: and when you press the abscess with your fingers, you feel as if it has a pulsation.
And that which is due to the vein is round on the surface of the body.
And incising this abscess is an error, especially when it is under the armpits, in the groin, on the neck, and in many parts of the body: and it is very serious. Therefore, its treatment should be avoided with iron, and those that are also in the extremities or on the head should be avoided as well.
Therefore, concerning that which comes from the swelling of the artery's opening, make an incision in the skin lengthwise. Then open the incision with hooks, then the artery: and free it from the tunics, until it is exposed.
Then insert a needle under it, and make it penetrate all the way to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread at two places, according to what I taught you in extracting the two arteries which are in the temples.
Then puncture the area between the two ligatures with a lancet until all the blood within it escapes and the abscess is resolved.
Then apply treatment that generates pus until the ligatures fall off: afterwards treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
If the abscess is due to the cutting of a vein, then you must hold as much of the abscess with the skin as you can with your hand. Then insert a needle under the area you are holding with your hand, and make it penetrate: and have double thread on it until you pull it out from the other side. Then tie it with a good bandage along with the abscess: according to what I told you about tying a grape, from both sides with both ends of the thread.
If you fear that the thread will be pulled out, then insert another needle with another thread under the entire abscess at the needle's incision: press and tie your threads at four places.
Then cut the abscess in its middle until what is inside comes out; then cut away the excess skin, and leave what was bound from it.
Then place on it the poultice which you soaked in wine and oil. Then administer the treatment which is done with plasters and ointments until it heals.
Chapter L.
Regarding the abscess that occurs from the twisting of nerves.
As an abscess occurs in arteries and veins, so does an abscess occur in nerves: which happens to them through percussion or from excessive labor and similar causes: and it is most common in places such as the helpers, or heel, and in any place where joints are moved: and this abscess is severe.
Its color resembles the rest of the body, and it is in most cases without pain: and when it is pressed with vehemence, the patient feels something similar to stupor in it.
And the abscess is not aggregated deep within the body, but it is beneath the skin, and it can be moved in all directions, nor does it go forward or backward to the rear.
Therefore, what is among them in the joints should not be penetrated with iron. For it may cause contraction.
In those that are in the head or forehead, incise the skin with a spatula. If therefore it is a small abscess, then hold it with tweezers, and cut it off from the root.
And if it is large, then hang it with a hook, and remove the skin: then take it away, and close the wound with stitches: and care for it until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-One.
On the incision of an abscess that occurs in the abdomen.
There occur in some men at times in their bellies, and in the rest of their bodies, growths which are called Fungalia, by similarity to fungi.
Whose root is subtle, and their head is thick, and their lips are inverted. And some of them are small: and some of them become greatly enlarged.
And I have indeed seen a man, and in his belly were two growths, which were more like fungi than other things: there was no difference between them, they were white, of small roots, and their lips were inverted, and they ended, and moisture ran from them always.
I cut them, and found one to weigh nearly ten and eight ounces and the other nearly six ounces. The procedure for cutting them is such that you should then consider if the patient is moist, and the color of the growth is white, moist, and of a subtle root: then cut it with a broad spatula, and have cauterizations ready at hand over fire.
For often much blood is expelled upon cutting it: therefore hurry if the blood overcomes you, then cauterize it.
If you see the patient fearful and timid about being cut with iron, then take a properly made thread of lead, and bind it to the athelul: whose amount is as we have said, and leave it for two days.
Then add to the binding of lead. Therefore, do not cease to bind the lead whenever it adheres to the hair, until it is separated and falls off by itself without effort.
If the hair has a thick root, then there is something to fear and be anxious about its cutting: especially when it is on the belly.
However, it is possible to cut through the middle of it. Then cauterize it so that it does not return.
Then care for it until the wound heals.
And beware lest you presume to cut the hair which is of black color, little sensation, ugly appearance: for it is a cancerous tumor; and I will come with a reminder of Cancer after this.
Chapter LII.
Concerning the treatment of the navel protrusion.
The protrusion of the navel occurs for many reasons. Or from the fissures of the sifac, which is above the belly: and althub or intestine comes out of it, according to what happens in other hernias. Or from the blood that flows from a vein or an artery, according to what has been previously stated. Or from constrained wind in it.
If however it is due to a sifac fissure, and the exit of thirbi: then the color of the apostema is similar to the color of the body: and it is gentle, without pain: and appears at different sites. And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then its location is of much greater diversity than what we have mentioned. When you press it with your fingers, it disappears: then it returns, and perhaps there is a sound with it: and it swells greatly at the entrance of the bath, and causes great labor.
If it is due to moisture, it is gentle, then it does not disappear when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrict or increase.
If it is due to blood, then the apostema appears with these signs towards blackness from the slope.
If it is due to born flesh: then the apostema is heavy, thick, hard, and fixed according to one quantity.
If it is due to wind, then its touch is gentle.
And the operation in this case is to determine if the prominence of the navel is due to blood from an Artery, or Vein, or wind: then you must refrain from treating it. For in this case there is fear and dread, as I taught you in the chapter where I said about apostemata due to artery and vein.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to the intestine or the zhiri: then it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold their breath and stand stretched. Then mark with encaustic around the entire navel. Then instruct him to lie supine in your hands on his back. Then circle with a broad spatula around the navel on the place which you marked with encaustic. Then extend the middle of the abscess upward with a large hook. Then bind him firmly around the circumference with thread or with silk cord: and let the knot of the binding be secure.
Then open the extended middle of the abscess above the binding. If you find it already captured by the binding: then extract securely, and insert your index finger into it, and push the intestine into the abdomen: and if you find the zhiri, then take it with a hook, and cut off its excess.
If however an artery or vein is in the way: then tie it tightly. Then return to your operation. And take two needles, and insert two strong threads into them: and insert the two needles around the area you made around the abscess in the shape of a cross, which you make to penetrate.
Then grasp the abscess at four points above the needles: and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave the area until the extended flesh putrefies: and falls off by itself: or cut it when it becomes thin and putrid.
Then care for it with what is necessary from ointments until it is healed.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to hard flesh in it or moisture, then it is necessary to hollow out the abscess as we have said. And you shall remove the blood or moisture that you find in it.
Then care for it with what strengthens the area.
Chapter LIII.
About the treatment of CANCER.
We have already spoken about the classification of cancer types and how to treat it with medicines. And one must be cautious when treating it with surgery so that it does not become ulcerated. We have also discussed cancer generated in the uterus and precautions for its treatment.
And the ancients said that sometimes cancer is in a place where its removal is possible, such as cancer in the breasts or in the thigh and similar limbs located for extracting it entirely, especially when it is a small, initial growth.
When it is old and large, you should not approach it closely.
For I was not able to heal anyone from it, nor have I seen anyone before me who has succeeded in treating it.
And the procedure for it, when it is located as we have said, is to precede and relieve the patient from black bile several times. Then bleed it if you find it with obvious fullness.
Then prepare the patient for the preparation in which he is placed with the operation.
Then throw into the cancer hooks that suit it. Then hollow it out from all sides with the skin according to the examination until nothing remains of its roots: and let the blood flow, and do not cut it quickly, but press the areas, and wipe off all the thick blood with your hand, or with whatever is possible there from the instruments.
If, however, the flow of thick blood from the incision of an artery or vein opposes you, then cauterize the vein until the blood is stopped. Then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
Regarding the treatment of dropsy.
Chapter LIIII. We have already discussed in the division the types of dropsy, and how the gathering of water occurs: and the signs of each type, and its treatment with medicines.
And that which is treated with iron is only the ascites type alone: and it is not approached with iron in the case of the tympanites type: nor thoroughly in the case of the hyposarca type: for that is deadly.
When you have already treated this type of dropsy, tympanites, with medicines and your treatment has not helped: then consider. For if the patient has already incurred weakness, or there is another illness with them besides dropsy: such as if they have a cough, or diarrhea, and similar conditions: then beware of treating them with iron: for there is fear in that.
If however you see a patient with excess strength, and he has no illness other than dropsy alone: and he is neither a child nor an old person: then the method of treatment in his case is that you lift the patient standing between your hands, and the assistant behind him should press his belly with his hand driving the water to the lower part of the chest.
Then take the spiked spatula according to this shape. Let it be of two sharp parts, long, with a sharp end like a spatula. However, let there be something of gradual shortness in it, so that you do not penetrate through it during the operation all the way to the intestine and injure it.
Then consider. For if the cause of dropsy is from the intestines, then it is necessary to extend with the incision three fingers' width below the navel, towards the lower part directly above the pubic region.
If however the cause of dropsy is due to disease of the liver: then let your incision be to the left of the navel by three fingers.
And if its cause is due to the spleen, then the incision should be on the right side: and it should not be on the side on which the patient prefers to lie, so that the excess fluids do not flow to that weak spot.
Then pierce the skin entirely with the instrument. Then insert into that incision, and lift your hand with the spatula between the skin, and sinew, as if you are flaying it: and let the amount flayed be the size of a nail, or about that.
Then pierce the sinus until the spatula reaches the empty space: and that is the location of the water. Then extract it, and insert into the opening an instrument which has this form. And it is like a cannula: made of silver, or bronze, or brass, smooth, clean: which has at its lower part a small opening, and on its sides are three openings, two from one side, and one from the other side: and the edge is its cut end according to the manner of cutting a reed, as you see: at its upper end is a ring.
For when the instrument reaches the water, then it descends immediately on the instrument, therefore evacuate the amount of water in an hour.
For if you evacuate more than is appropriate from it in an hour, the patient may die through the dissolution of his animal spirit, or he may suffer a syncope that approaches death.
But evacuate from it according to the quantity of its power, and according to what the dispositions of the patient signify to you from the strength of his pulse, and from his good condition.
Then remove the instrument, and retain the water.
This is because it is retained immediately due to the skin which holds the opening that is on the sinus: of which I have spoken, so that you pierce it in that manner.
Then insert the instrument again on the next day, if you see the patient tolerate it: and also extract a small amount of water.
Do that for several days without fear, and guard yourself from error: until hardly any water remains.
If you are afraid for the patient and leave much water behind: then treat him with burial in warm sand, and much sweating in a bath and sun, and expect thirst: and treat him with drying medicines until he is healed: and cauterize over the stomach, spleen, and liver after the extraction of water: as I have narrated in what precedes.
On the care of infants who are born with unperforated urine passages.
Chapter Fifty-Five.
When one of the infants exits the womb of his mother, and his anus is not perforated, or there is a narrow opening, or it is not in its proper place.
Therefore, it is necessary to intervene with the perforation immediately upon birth using a very fine spatula, according to this method.
Then place a thin pin made of lead in the opening and tie it: and keep it there for three days, or four.
When he wants to urinate, it should be removed, and he may urinate. Then replace it.
And if you do not place the lead, it is possible that the urine which flows over the area will prevent it from closing.
He whose opening is narrow is treated with lead, as we have said, for many days until it is enlarged.
Those who have a hole in an unusual place are injured. Which is because, in those who are born, there is a hole at the end of the penis: therefore, he cannot urinate forward until he lifts the penis upward with his hand. He cannot reproduce because the sperm cannot reach the womb properly: and it is a very foul disease.
And the method of the operation is to lay the patient on their back. Then extend the head of his penis with your left hand strongly, and cut the head of the penis from the priapic area with a sharp knife or scalpel: like cutting a reed, or as if you were peeling something, so that its middle comes similar to the head of the penis: and so that the hole falls in the middle as it should.
And be careful during your operation from blood flow. For it often happens that. Therefore, apply to him something that stops the bleeding, and treat the wound until it heals.
Regarding Albather, which occurs in the foreskin and head of the penis, and concerning corruption, blackening, and adhering.
Chapter LVI.
These Albather often occur on the penis, and it is a foul flesh prominence.
And from it, some are malignant, and some are not malignant.
Therefore, you should suspend it with a subtle hook and cut it off until you clean it all. Then place on it a quince submerged in Egyptian ointment. Then treat it with diaphynction ointment after that until it heals.
If the Albather is malignant and of ugly color, then you should apply a cautery to it after its incision and reasoning.
If the Albather is in the foreskin of a captive, uncircumcised, and part of the Albather is within the foreskin and part of it outside: then you should remove the Albather that is inside first, until when it consolidates, then treat it externally: because when you treat them simultaneously, the foreskin does not heal without being stretched.
And it also happens in the testicles, and there is blackening and corruption in the foreskin. Therefore, you should scoop out everything that is already blackened and what is about to be corrupted or is already corrupted.
Then apply on it after that with honey which is already mixed with the flour of pomegranate rind and the herb of triturated sieve.
Then treat it with the remaining treatment until it heals.
If a flow of blood occurs, then apply a cautery with a crescent-shaped cautery, according to this form.
For cautery is beneficial for two conditions simultaneously, namely for blood flow and a wound when it becomes corrupted.
If the head of the penis is corroded and destroyed entirely within an hour: then it is necessary to insert a cannula made of lead into the urethra so that the patient may urinate over it.
In cases of the foreskin adhering to the head of the penis, and this adhesion does not occur unless in one whose foreskin is healthy and does not require circumcision: and sometimes it occurs due to a wound or an abscess: therefore, it is necessary to scrape it with a blunt spatula until the bond is loosened and the head of the penis is freed on all sides.
If it is difficult to distinguish them precisely, then it is necessary to scrape away something from the head of the penis and from the foreskin. This is because the foreskin, when it is thin, may be punctured quickly due to its thinness.
Then separate the foreskin from the head of the penis with a fine linen cloth that has already been moistened in cold water, so that they do not stick together again.
Then it should be treated with astringent wine until it is healed.
Chapter LVII.
Regarding the cleansing of infants and the treatment of errors that befall them.
Circumcision is not a solution for continuity like other wounds; however, since it is performed by our operation, by our will, and its use is proper for children, it is necessary to mark it with a better procedure and an easier path leading to healing.
Therefore, I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision in any of their books: because they do not use it in their laws, and it is only what we have acquired through experience.
Which is because I found that the majority of surgeons and phlebotomists use purification by circumcision with a lancet and scissors: and they use cautery, binding with thread, and incision with a scalpel.
And I have indeed tested all these methods, and have not found a better one than purification with scissors and binding with thread.
Because in purification with a lancet, the skin often escapes. Because the skin of the foreskin has two layers: therefore, perhaps the upper layer is cut, and the lower layer remains: thus it is necessary to make another incision, causing future pain. And with the purification that is done by cautery, that is, digitally, which tailors use, the end of the male member is not secured from injury: because it might enter its opening.
In purification with a scalpel, the iron might slip and ruin your operation: and the skin of a boy is naturally short, and often they are born in such a way that they do not need purification: and I have already seen this.
However, the method of purification with scissors and binding with thread has proven to be good through experience: because scissors are proportional in their cutting: therefore, the sharpness on top is like the sharpness below. When therefore you press with your hand, two sharpnesses are proportioned, and they fall according to one operation at the same time: and a compression of similar shape is made, containing the skin of the rod from all sides, with which no error at all occurs.
And the method of the operation is to make the boy understand, especially if he is one of those who grasp quickly, that you do nothing except tie a thread to his rod only: and leave him until another day.
Then make him rejoice and be glad in every way that is possible for you to do so, from what his own understanding receives. Then make him stand between your prepared hands, and let him not be sitting: and hide the scissors in your sleeve, or under your foot, so that the boy does not see them at all, nor any of the instruments.
Then insert your hand to his rod, and blow on the skin, and pull it up until the head of the rod comes out. Then cleanse it from what dirt accumulates on it.
Then bind the marked area with a double thread. Then bind below that briefly with a second bandage. Then hold with your index finger and thumb the area of the lower bandage firmly, and cut between the two bandages. Then pull the skin up quickly, and extract the head of the rod. Then let the blood flow gradually (for it is better) and apply powder on top: and on top of the powder place a cloth in which an egg yolk beaten in rose water, mixed with good fresh rose oil, is spread: and leave it on until another day: and care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
The form of the scissors for cleaning is this.
Let the two ends be blunt and inclined so that the branch of the nail does not protrude from them: and let the length of the two sharp parts be equal to the length of the two handles.
The error falling in cleaning is: because perhaps the inner skin entirely or part of it escapes at the incision.
Therefore, it is necessary to extend it with your thumb before the apostemation of the area: and cut it according to equality.
If you cannot hold it with your thumb, then extract it with a hook, and cut it.
If however three days have passed and what is under the nail remains swollen, having formed an abscess: then leave it until the hot abscess ripens, and remove the scab with ease, and cut it according to how it is prepared for you: and beware of the tip of the nail. For it will not harm it.
Treat it with what consolidates the wound from the powders we mentioned in the section on powders: and if it is cut beyond measure from the skin and extends to the upper parts, it will not harm it either.
Treat it with what we have said until it heals.
Chapter LVIII.
Regarding the extraction of retained urine in the bladder.
Retention of urine in the bladder occurs from an obstruction caused by a stone, or coagulated blood, or pus, or flesh growths, and similar things from those methods of treatment we have mentioned in the division.
And if the urine is not resolved, and you see that its retention is due to a Stone already in the neck of the bladder: then it is necessary for the patient to be bent over on his knees. Then his feet should be placed on his back, and he should extend his abdomen from the upper part of his back, and the patient should hold his breath as much as possible. Therefore, the neck of the bladder is forced to expel the Stone towards the back: hence the urine is released.
If it is not resolved by what we have said, and the matter is severely affecting the patient: then it is necessary to administer its extraction with an instrument which is called a syringe, whose form is as follows: It should be made of silver, and be delicate, soft, hollow like the tube of a bird's feather in the thinness of a finger, long resembling one and a half palms: with a fine tube at its head.
And the method of urine exiting through it is to take a doubled thread, and tie wool or cotton, a good ligature, at its end: and insert the end of the thread into the lower part of the syringe: and cut with scissors if there is any excess wool, but insert it into the tube forcefully, like an awl.
Then anoint the syringe with oil, or with butter, and egg white: and have the patient sit on a seat, and insert the syringe into the bladder, and its rod with wet oils, and olive oil, and warm water.
Then insert the syringe into the twig with ease until it reaches the root of the twig.
Then double it above the navel.
Then insert the syringe into it until it reaches the bladder, and let the patient feel that it has already reached the empty place: and this is not done in this order unless because the passage through which it goes is twisted.
Then extend the thread with wool gradually. For the abscess will follow the wool.
Then remove it, and make the abscess flow through the urine passage: and repeat the syringe, and do not stop doing this until the bladder is emptied, and the patient finds relief.
Regarding the quality of bladder irrigation with a clepsydra.
Chapter LIX.
When an ulcer occurs in the bladder, or blood congeals in it, or pus is compressed in it, and you wish to distill water and medicines into it: then it should be done with an instrument called a clepsydra, and this is its form.
For it is closed, that is, sealed. And in it there are three holes, two on one side, and one on the other side, as you see.
And the concave area, in which is the part that pushes, should be according to the size that fits it without addition, until when something is drawn with it, moisture is attracted: and when it is pushed, it expels the moisture far away: as a clepsydra does, from which naphtha, that is, Greek fire, is projected in battles.
Therefore when you want to transfer moisture into the bladder, insert the end of the clepsydra into the moisture, and draw with it what is pushed upwards, for the moisture is drawn into the concavity of the clepsydra.
Then insert its end into the tube, as we have described in the syringe. Then push the moisture with that which pushes it, for that moisture reaches the bladder immediately, so that the patient feels it.
The form of a subtle clyster with which the bladder is irrigated.
Let it be made of silver or brass, whose head should be higher and similar to a small alcam, and below it there should be a groove in which the ligament falls.
Then take the bladder of a ram, and place in it the moisture with which you want to irrigate the bladder. Then tie it between two grooves with a strong ligature and double thread: and warm that moisture slightly over fire.
Then insert the end of the clyster into the tube, then place your hand over the bladder with the moisture in a proper grip, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
If you do not have a bladder available, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it entirely around its circumference. Then insert a strong thread into those holes, as they turn. Then add a circle, as is added to a brother: after you place on it what you wish from moistures, and oils, and waters.
Then bind it to the instrument: and do with it as you did with the bladder by pressing with your hand, until the moisture reaches the bladder.
Chapter LX.
Regarding the extraction of Stone.
We have already discussed the classification of stone types and its treatment with medicines: and I mentioned the difference between a stone generated in the kidneys and bladder, and the signs of it all: and I spoke of the stone on which manual operation and incision falls: and this is the stone properly generated in the bladder: and that which is fixed in the penis: and I am narrating this with clear explanation and abbreviation.
I say, therefore, that the stone generated in the bladder most often occurs in children.
And among its signs is that urine exits the bladder similar to water in its fineness: and white sand appears in it, and the patient rubs his penis, and labors with it, and hangs down frequently. Then it erects, and the anus exits with it in many of them.
And the healing is easy for children up until they reach fourteen years. And it is difficult in the elderly. In young adults it is moderate, between the two extremes: and for those whose stone is larger, the treatment is easier: and if smaller, the treatment is conversely more difficult.
When we come to the treatment, it is first necessary that we cleanse the patient with a purgative which removes all the feces that are in his intestines: for it sometimes prevents the discovery of the Stone during the examination.
Then the patient should be taken with his feet and shaken and moved downward: so that the Stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, or jumps from a height several times.
Then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be under his hips, so that the bladder becomes entirely inclined downward.
Then examine him, and touch him externally.
If you feel the Stone in the space, then immediately proceed with the incision over it.
If it does not yield entirely to your touch, then you must clean your index finger with the oil of your left hand if the patient is a boy: or your middle finger if he is a full-grown youth: and insert it into his anus, and search for the Stone until it stands under your finger: and gradually turn it towards the neck of the bladder.
Then press on it with your finger, and drive it outward toward the site where you wish to make the incision: and command one servant to press the bladder with his hand, and command another servant to lift the testicles upward with his right hand: and with his other hand, to pull away the skin that is beneath the testicles from the site of the incision.
Then insert the Spatumile for cutting, which has this form. And find what is between the anus and the testicles, and not in the middle, to the left side of the buttocks: and let the incision be above the stone, and your finger be in the anus: and let the incision be transverse, so that the cut be wider on the outside and narrower on the inside, according to the amount that the exit of the Stone from it should not be larger.
For perhaps the finger which is in the anus compresses the Stone near the incision, and it exits without difficulty.
And know that the Stone has angles and edges, which is why its exit is difficult because of that.
And it is smooth, similar to a gland, and round: and its exit is easy.
Therefore, for the one that has angles and edges, add to the incision.
If it does not exit thus, then you must be ingenious with it: either grasp it with forceps properly, the end of which is like a crescent, which grasps on the Stone and does not slip away from it: or insert beneath it a subtle instrument of curved end.
If you cannot grasp it, then enlarge the opening slightly. If anything from the blood overpowers you, cut it with a scissors.
If there is more than one stone, then push the larger one towards the bladder opening first. Then make an incision over it. Then push the smaller one after that: and do likewise if there are more than two.
If it is very large, then it is ignorance to cut a large incision on it. For it happens to the sick person one of two things, either that he dies or there is a continuous distillation of urine; therefore, because the place is not consolidated at all.
But administer the expulsion of it until it comes out: or extract the fragments of its fracture with scissors until you remove it piece by piece.
Therefore, when you have completed the operation, then fill the wound with frankincense, aloe, and dragon's blood: and bind it, and place over it cloth soaked in oil and wine, or rose oil, and cold water: so that the warm pus may be set.
Then place the sick person on their back, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day. Therefore, when you loosen it, fumigate the area with water and much oil.
Then treat it with diaphyllite ointment and basilicon ointment until it heals.
If, however, a warm pus and corroded matter, and things similar to those, happen in the wound: such as if blood congeals in the bladder and urine is prevented by it: and this is known by the discharge of blood with urine. Therefore, insert your finger into the wound and extract that blood. For if it remains, it causes the corruption of the bladder and its putrefaction.
Then wash the wound with vinegar, and water, and salt: and treat every type as befits its treatment until it is healed.
And it is necessary during the entire course of treatment to bind the two hips together, for the sake of the medicines that are placed on the area.
If the stone is small and is in the channel of the penis, and is fixed there, and the passage of urine is prevented: then treat it with what I narrate before you reach the incision. For often you will be spared from surgery through this treatment, for I have already proven it.
And it is such that you take the Perforatorium from Alferac iron, whose form is this, with a triangular tip, sharp, fixed in wood.
Then take a string and tie the penis with it under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
Then insert the perforating iron into the penis with ease until the Perforatorium reaches the stone itself: and turn the Perforatorium with your hand on the stone gradually: and strive to penetrate it until you make it go through the other side.
For the urine is immediately expelled.
Then press your hand on what remains of the stone from the outer part of the penis. For it breaks apart and exits with the urine, and the patient is healed.
If this treatment is not prepared for you, because of something that prevents it: then tie a string under the stone and another string above the stone. Then cut on the stone on the twig between the two ligatures. Then extract it. Then loosen the ligature, and clean the clotted blood that forms in the wound.
And it is not necessary to tie the thread under the stone unless it does not return to the bladder: and another ligature above, unless when the thread is loosened after the exit of the stone, the skin returns to its place and covers the wound: and for this reason you must do it when you tie the upper thread, to raise the skin upwards, so that it returns at the completion and covers the wound, as we have said.
Chapter LXI.
Regarding the extraction of stones in women.
A stone is rarely generated in women.
If, however, it happens that any of them has a stone, then the treatment is difficult, and it is prohibited due to many reasons.
One of the reasons is that the woman may be a virgin.
And the second is that you do not find a woman who will expose herself to a doctor when she is chaste, or among those who have husbands.
The third is that you do not find a woman well skilled in this art, especially the manual procedure.
And the fourth is the distance from the location of the stone: therefore, it requires deep incision, and there is fear in that.
If necessity provokes to this, then it is necessary that you take a female doctor, well knowledgeable: and she is rarely found.
If you are deprived of that, then seek a pure and skilled doctor, and present a well-educated midwife in women's affairs, or a woman who shows some part of the skill in this art: therefore make her present, and especially instruct her to do everything you command her according to the examination on the stone.
First of all, it is to see if the woman is a virgin: then he must insert a finger into her anus, and seek the stone.
If he finds it, he should press it under his finger, and then instruct the midwife to insert her finger into the vulva of the patient, and examine over the stone, after placing her left hand on the bladder, and pressing it with a good compression.
If he finds the stone, then it is necessary that he gradually move it from the opening of the bladder downward with all his strength until he reaches the root of the hip with it.
Then he should incise over it at the midpoint of the vulva near the root of the hip, on whichever side is prepared for him, and where he feels the stone: and his finger should not be removed from the stone, pressing under it; and the incision should be small at first. Then he should insert a probe over that incision.
Then he should insert a probe over that incision. If he feels the stone, then he should increase the incision according to the amount proportional to how the stone is exiting from it.
And know that there are many kinds of stones. From these there is a small one and a large one, smooth and rough, long and round having branches.
Know therefore its kinds, so that it may be signified to you through this about what you desire.
If therefore the blood overcomes you, then add in place of zegi powder, and hold it for one hour, until the blood is stopped.
Then return to your operation until the stone comes out: and do so that you prepare with you from the instruments I mentioned for extracting stones in men, to assist you with them in your operation.
If the flow of blood overcomes you, and you know that the expulsion of blood is from the artery which has been cut: then place powder on the area, and bind it with bandages tightly: and do not change it: and leave the stone, and do not extract it. For perhaps the weak woman may die. Then treat the wound.
When therefore the sharpness of the blood is calmed after days, and the place becomes putrefied, then return to your operation until the stone comes out.
Chapter LXII.
Regarding the incision of a watery hernia.
A watery ramex is not such unless it is an aggregation of moisture in the sifac alb, which is beneath the skin of the testicle containing the egg: and it is called sifac.
And sometimes it is in its own membrane, which nature has prepared for it in the part of the egg, until it is considered: which is another kind of egg, and it is the skin of the testicle between the white, which we have said: and that does not occur except rarely.
And the generation of this ramification is from the weakness which befalls the testicles: whence this material is discharged to them. And sometimes it happens from a blow upon the testicles.
And this moisture has many colors. For its color is either inclined to yellow, or it is blood red, or bile-like black, or it is water-like white, and this is what predominates.
And the signs by which it is known where the aggregation of water is, are these. For if it is in the white part which we have said, then the abscess is round in length somewhat like the shape of an egg: and the testicle does not appear, because the moisture contains it on all sides.
And if the moisture is in its own membrane, then the abscess is round with a part of the egg, and because of this, a person thinks that it is another egg.
And if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white part, then it falls under sensation.
When therefore you wish to know the color of the moisture, then test the color of the moisture in the abscess with an inserted square, whose form preceded. According to what goes out in the track of the Intromissi, judge of that which is within it.
Therefore, when we come to the treatment with iron, then it is necessary that you advise the patient to be bled if it is possible for him, and you see his body full.
Then he should lie on his back on something slightly elevated, and place many cloths under him.
Then sit on his left, and instruct the assistant to sit on his right, who will stretch his rod to one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles, and to the groin area.
Then take a broad scalpel, and cut the skin of the testicles lengthwise through the middle, nearly to the epididymis: and let the incision be made according to a straight equidistant line that divides the skin of the testicles, until it reaches the white membrane enclosing it: and strip it off, and observe, beware from this so as not to cut it yourself: and let your stripping be on the part which hangs more with the egg: and carefully examine with the stripping according to what is possible for you.
Then pierce the membrane full of water with a wide puncture, and draw out all the water.
Then separate the two lips of the incision with forceps, and extend the membrane upward, and do not touch the skin enclosing the testicles: and cut the membrane however it is possible for you to cut it, either entirely or piece by piece, especially its thin side. For if you do not examine it thoroughly, security is not achieved in the incision, lest the water returns.
If however the egg comes out from its skin during your operation time: then when you have completed the cutting, reduce it back. Then sew together the two edges of the skin of the testicles.
Then care for it like other wounds until it heals.
If you find the egg corrupted by blackening or other [signs], then it is necessary to tie the vessels, which are the spermatic cords, fearing blood flow.
Then cut off the testicle with the spermatic cord, and extract the egg: afterwards care for it as we have said.
If water has gathered in two parts, then know that there are two branches: therefore cut the other part equally as you did in the other.
And if it seems to you that the operation is one, then do as follows: afterwards clean the blood. And insert into the incisions wool soaked in oil, or in rose oil: and place outside another piece of wool which you have soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over both testicles, and the abdominal area: and place a double cloth on top, and these are poultices: and bind them with a bandage that has six layers according to this form.
Then let two cloths be taken, and sweated, and filled with ground laudanum according to this likeness: and the ends by which it is pressed should be of felt or damp wool: and they should be bound with a band around the waistband of the breeches: and one end should cover from the anus up to the back, and the second cover the hip area: and the two ends above should be on both thighs below, and the other two ends should be over the two groins, and the entire band should be bound around the waistband of the breeches.
And sometimes this is treated artificially with a cautery instead of cutting with iron: and it is that you take a subtle knife-like cautery, and cut with it the skin of the testicles: and it is ignited as we have narrated: until when the white membrane containing water is revealed: then take the cautery according to this form.
It is assimilated to the Greek letter.
Then pierce that membrane with it, and it is ignited until all the moisture comes out.
Then extend the membrane with hooks, and remove the skin with a subtle ignited cautery, and cut it as much as you can until you root out all of it.
And be careful with the egg, that fire does not touch it.
And know that this operation is safer, involves less bleeding, and is better than the operation with cutting.
If, however, something opposes you at the time of cutting or cauterizing, such as a warm swelling, or bleeding, or anything else: then you must treat what opposes you with the cure that is suitable to it, according to what has been mentioned.
If, however, the patient is timid and does not endure this operation due to its horror: then administer the piercing as I describe it: and it is done.
When it is confirmed to you through what we have said about the signs that the ramex is watery: then you must make the patient sit on an elevated seat.
Then pierce the abscess on its lower part with a broad spatula: and place the puncture according to the length of the body, and let the opening be wide, until all the water flows out.
Then place a cup over the area, and bind it, and leave it so that the remaining water may flow out; then care for it until the wound heals.
If opposition occurs to the flow of water when you pierce it: and if this is only because the white membrane causes opposition at the wound's opening and prevents the exit of water: then it is necessary to insert a feather into the wound, or an instrument with which the water of dropsy is extracted, whose form has been mentioned before: or temporarily add to the operation of the wound.
And know that the water returns and gathers after six months, or around that time. When it gathers again, then it should be punctured in the same manner, and the patient will pass his days.
Chapter LXIII.
Regarding the treatment of fleshy branches.
Know that in the cutting of this fleshy branch, there is fear-leading-to-destruction in many conditions. Therefore, it seems to me that its removal is salvaging from it.
And I am recalling the procedure on it and the nature of the abscess.
I say, therefore, that many abscesses occur in the bodies from which the testicles are formed: and this happens for many reasons, namely.
Or from sharp and bitter excess, which is poured out toward the testicles. Or from a blow.
And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body, and no pain is found in it: and it is a heavy abscess.
And perhaps it is a stony abscess, whose color is dark, and there is no sensation in it.
And sometimes it occurs from the knotting of arteries and their swelling: as has already been mentioned beforehand: or from the swelling of veins.
That which is from the swelling of arteries is recognized by the condition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers. And you should not touch it at all.
That which occurs from the swelling of veins does not spread anything upon compression with fingers.
And now it is possible to perform surgery on this type and on the other flesh: and it is as if you were to cut the skin of the testicles. Then extend the egg upward, and extract it with a white cloth: and free the suspensory ligament from the vessels, and tie the vessels: and cut the suspensory ligament after you free it from all parts of the egg.
If the egg is consolidated with those born flesh, then you must pull the egg and cut it.
And if there is adhesion between something in the scrotum or among the vessels: then you must free that entire adhesion and cut it with a circular incision.
If however there is flesh growth in the area of attachment which is behind: then it is necessary to cut out all of it and remove the egg as we have said.
When therefore your operation is complete, then fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine: then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
Chapter LXIIII.
About the treatment of shoots, which is done with vines.
Vitis is an apostem wrapped in a certain convolution, similar to a botryoid, with a softening of the testicles: and it makes movement and exercise difficult for the patient, as well as walking.
And in the treatment of this illness, there is fear, because of that which preceded and was remembered.
But it is necessary, as we say, to perform the operation according to what the first practitioners did.
I say therefore that it is necessary to have the patient sit on an elevated seat. Then push the suspension of the testicles downward. Then hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, near the tubes: and let another assistant hold and stretch them vigorously.
Then make a transverse cut with a broad and sharp spatula directly across the tubes until the tubes are exposed.
Then remove the outer layer from all sides, as we have told you in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples.
Then insert into them a needle on which there is double thread, and tie it at the first place where the Vines are injured: and tie it again at the last of them. Then cut them in the middle section straight according to the length of the body, and remove what gathers from corrupted feculent humidities.
Then treat the wound with the treatment of other wounds, in which you generate pus, so that the vessels which nourish one of the testicles fall. For it is not evil through that.
If the Vines happen to all vessels, then it is necessary that the testicles be removed with the vessels: so that the egg is not deprived of nourishment because of the incision, and wastes away, or dries up, and is not beneficial with them.
Chapter sixty-five.
Regarding the treatment of intestinal branches.
The outcome of this branching is from the incision that occurs in the extended sifach over the belly in the groin area from the mirach of the belly.
Therefore, the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles. And this rupture is either from the sifach or its extension.
And these two types occur from many causes: either from a blow, or jumping, or shouting, or lifting a heavy object, and the like.
And the sign is when it is from the extension of the sifach. It happens gradually over a long period of time and does not happen suddenly: and it is an abscess equal towards the depth: therefore, the sifach compresses the intestine.
And the sign of it when it is from the section of sifach, because it causes a violent pain suddenly at the beginning: and it is a different abscess, appearing near under the skin: and this is due to the exit of the intestine, and its course to the outer parts of sifach.
And sometimes it exits with the intestine zirbum: and this is named Intestinal Ramex, and zirbia: and sometimes it occurs with flatulence.
And sometimes the feces run into the intestine and are retained there: and it is harmful to the patient: for it causes severe pain, especially when it is compressed.
And in the treatment of this kind of illness with iron there is fear: therefore, one must be cautious about accidents in it.
And the method of the operation is to instruct the patient to draw the intestine with his hand into the depths of his own concavity, if it obeys the return. Then he should lie on his back with his neck between your hands: and lift his legs.
Then extend the skin that follows upward, and cut the entire skin of the testicles lengthwise. Then insert hooks into the two lips of the incision as needed to open the incision with them: and the incision should be of such quantity that it is possible for the egg to exit from it.
Then excoriate the saphakh, and what is under the skin of the testicles, until when the white saphakh is revealed, hard on all sides: then insert your index finger into what follows the testicle, into what is between the white saphakh, which is under the skin of the scrotum, and between the second saphakh, and completely separate the adhesion which is in the posterior part of the scrotum.
Then move with your right hand the skin of the testicles towards the inside: and at the same time stretch the white saphakh upwards with your left hand: and lift the egg with the saphakh to the part of the incision: and command the servant to stretch the egg upwards: and you loosen the adhesion which is at the back upon completion of the separation.
And seek with your fingers that there be nothing there of the intestine wrapped in the hard white saphakh. If you find anything of it: then push it downwards towards the abdomen.
