Then take a needle with thick thread, made of lynx from ten threads: and insert it near the last saphakh, that is, the tunic which is under the skin of the testicles following the incision: then cut the ends that protrude from the thread until there are four threads. Then arrange some of them over some in the shape of a cross: and tie with them the alsifach, of which we spoke, because it is under the skin of the testicles firmly tied, until none of the vessels that nourish them can send anything to them: so that a warm abscess does not result from it. And place the second ligature outside the first ligature, less than two fingers away from it. And after these two ligaments release from the scrotum, which is under the skin of the testicles, a quantity of the size of a finger: and cut all the remainder according to the roundness, and remove the egg from it.
Then cut at the lower part of the skin of the testicles where blood and pus flow: as we have narrated in what has been mentioned before.
Then apply wool soaked in oil, and place it on the wound: and apply the bandage as we have narrated. And sometimes the white scrotum that we mentioned is cauterized after its incision, fearing a flow of blood. For it often happens. And release the bandage until it falls off by itself.
If its falling off is delayed, then bathe it with warm water: and place on it what we have said, until it falls off.
Then treat the wound with the rest of the treatment for wounds, until it is healed.
Chapter LXVI.
Regarding the windy arm.
In this windy arm, I have not seen anyone who has dared to attempt its treatment with iron.
And at first, they said that it happens as we have narrated in the arm that is with the vine. Which is to bind the vessels after cutting and easily apply something over them: then cut in the middle, and finally treat it with what opens it until the vessels fall: and treat the wound as we have said, until it heals.
Chapter LXVII.
Of the tear which occurs in the groin.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the place protrudes, and nothing of the intestines descends to the testicles: and if it does descend, it is little, and returns at all times: but if time is prolonged with it, a fissure is added in the scrotum, until the intestines descend into the scrotum.
And it happens from the extension of the scrotum, which is in the groin, as we have said. Which means that the scrotum is extended; then it softens, and the place becomes inflamed and protrudes.
And its treatment is with a cautery, as was previously described.
And sometimes it is treated with an iron, in this manner: and it is that the patient lies on his back under your hands. Then cut the place of the ruptured and protruding inflammation with a horizontal incision, according to the width of three fingers.
Then grasp the scrotum and what is under the skin until the white membrane that is under the following skin is revealed.
Then take the probe and place it on the protruding part of the scrotum, and press it deeply towards the abdomen.
Then sew the two protruding areas above the end of the probe through the scrotum together with a suture; then remove the end of the probe.
And do not cut into the bladder at all, nor stretch the eye, nor anything else, as I have made you know in the treatment of intestinal branches.
Then treat it with the treatment of wounds. When you cut the threads, clean it, and restore the wound until it solidifies.
For sisach is contracted, and no prominence is added to the rupture.
And the cautery is better in this place: because it is nearer to healing.
Chapter LXVIII.
On the softening of the skin of the testicles.
The skin of the testicles is often softened in some men, because of which the flesh between them is also softened, and its appearance is marred.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one who is asked to treat it to make the patient lie on their back and cut away all the skin that has been softened down to the natural skin.
Then bring together the two lips with a suture: and if you wish, first remove the excess of the softened skin with three or four stitches, and secure the suture.
Then cut between the sutures.
Then treat it with the treatment of other wounds until it heals and the threads fall out.
Chapter LXIX.
On Castration.
Know that castration is excommunicated by our law: and because of this it would be permissible for me to not remember it in my book: and there is no need to remember it, unless for the two methods.
One of which is that it should be known by the doctor when asked about it: and so that he may know its treatment for those to whom it happens.
And the other method is that we often need the castration of certain animals for our benefit through it, such as rams, goats, and cats, and similar animals.
I say therefore that castration is performed in two ways. Or by attrition. Or by making an incision and cutting.
In that which is done by attrition, the way of operation is: that we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles soften and loosen, and hang down: then rub them with your hand until they dissolve and do not appear under touch.
In castration by making an incision and cutting, you must hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then ligate the suspensorium, and cut above all the egg with one cut, until when two eggs come out: then incise them after you have defleshed each, and do not leave anything on them except a fine suture over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than that which is done by friction: for friction perhaps leaves something of the testicles, wherefore the animal desires intercourse.
Then care for the wound until it heals.
Chapter Seventy.
On the treatment of hermaphrodites of two types.
Hermaphrodites exist in two modes according to males. One of them is such that it appears in the space that follows, or in the skin of the testicles, in the area between the two testicles, in the shape of a female vulva, in which there are hairs: and sometimes urine flows from what is in the skin of the testicles.
In women, there is one type, and it is a female vulva above a comb-like structure entirely small, protruding outward: of which one is like a penis of a man, and two are like two testicles.
And the treatment for the three types, two from males and one type from females, is: because it is necessary to cut the additional flesh until the impression of them is removed. Then treat them with the treatment for other wounds.
In the second type of males, from which urine exits, which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment for it at all.
Chapter LXXI.
On the incision of tentigines and protruding flesh in women's vulvas.
A tent-like structure is perhaps added beyond what is natural, until it becomes ugly and its appearance is marred: and sometimes it grows so much in some women that it expands like in men, and extends to the point of intercourse.
Therefore, you must hold the excess of the tent-like structure with your hand or with a hook, and cut it: and do not hesitate in the incision, especially at the root: so that blood flow does not occur.
Then care for it with wound treatment until it heals.
The flesh that arises is the flesh that grows in the opening of the womb until it fills it: and it perhaps extends outward resembling a tail: and because of this, some first call the illness tailed. Therefore, we must cut it like we cut the tent-like structure, and treat it until it heals.
Regarding the treatment of Alratica, which is an unperforated female ulcer.
Chapter LXXII.
Alratica is when there is an unperforated female ulcer, or a small opening. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental alratica is caused by a preceding illness: and it occurs either from added flesh growth, or if fine, or thick: and it can occur either in the depth of the womb, or on its sides, or on its upper part, or lower part: and it prevents intercourse and conception, and childbirth, and perhaps even menstruation.
And knowledge of that is gained by the sight of the midwife, if apparent labor is near.
And if it is not apparent, then seek it with your fingers, or with a probe.
And if the labor is from a thin membrane and it is close to the two lips: then hurry and break it.
And it is as if you place eggs on the two lips.
Then place the index fingers of both your hands simultaneously, and let the woman lie on her back with her legs spread apart. Then extend the two lips with force until the thin membrane is broken and labor is opened.
Then take wool, and soak it in oil, and place it on the area: and let the woman sit every day so that the area does not become hardened differently.
And if the membrane is thick, dense: then it is necessary to cut it with a broad spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
And if the labor is from fleshy growths, then suspend it with hooks, and cut it: and let there be with you medicines that stop the flow of blood without mordancy, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and frankincense compounded with egg white.
Then administer a large lead cannula so that the wound does not heal quickly, keep it for several days: and apply lint from dry linen, then treat with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
And sometimes there is born in the matrix the birth of other flesh: therefore they must be cut according to this method: while there is no cancerous aposteme for a cancerous aposteme which is in the matrix, must not encounter iron at all.
Chapter LXXIII.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, Athehelil, and red Bothor in the ulcers of women.
Hemorrhoids are the opening of vein orifices, through which a great deal of blood flows continuously.
When therefore hemorrhoids become old, they turn into thelil: and I have already spoken about their types and signs: and here I will say which of them receive cure, and which do not.
I say, therefore, that hemorrhoids which are at the opening of the matrix and do not appear to the senses: then there is no cure for it with iron.
Those among them that are at the opening of the matrix and which can be sensed, are those that can be cured.
Therefore, you must introduce the woman into a cold room. Then extend the athehelil with scissors, or with a coarse cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then apply a powder over them at the flow of blood from one of the powders of lancing without mordancy: such as acacia, dragon's blood, frankincense, and similar substances.
Then press her feet against the wall for one hour. Then place it in cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumach, and pomegranate bark, and galls, and similar items.
Then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on her back.
If the blood is cut off with it, it is good: and if not, make suction cups adhere to the back, and teats, without scarification.
Then take wool, and soak it in the juice of tarathit, or the juice of arnoglossae, or the juice of alaulat branches, that is, agrimony, with Pontic wine, and make it adhere to the site.
When therefore the abscess quiets, then treat the area with ointments until it heals.
Albarth red is similar to the heads of alhaasse, and it has a rough appearance.
Therefore, you must cut what appears from it, according to what I said in thelil equally: and treat it until it heals.
Chapter LXXIIII.
Regarding the perforation of the uterus that occurs in the matrix.
Many types of abscesses occur in the matrix, such as cancer, stone abscess, ulcers, adubelati, alekilati, that is, herpes, aestiomemus, fistulas, hemorrhoids, ragadiae, thelil, and hot abscess.
And I indeed have already said all these diseases and their kinds, and their signs, and their cures in the division: it is necessary that I speak in this treatise of the warm abscess which occurs in the uterus, when it is among the abscesses that collect pus, and you wish to know how its opening is made with iron.
Therefore, you must consider. Then if the pain of the abscess in its beginning is sharp with its percussion, and flame, and fever: and you see it reddening: if sensation fails over it, then do not hurry with its puncture: and treat it with what aids maturation until when the acuteness of the symptoms subsides.
Then it is necessary that you make the woman sit on a seat which slopes to two seats, and recline, or lie down on her back, and draw her feet together toward the lower part of the belly: and let her thighs be spread apart, and place her arms under her knees, and bind each with a suitable band.
Then let the midwife sit on the right side and administer the instrument with which the womb's opening is pierced.
And it is necessary when you wish to administer this instrument, that you insert with the sound the depth of the woman's womb: so that what enters from the instrument is not deeper than the depth of the womb, and injure the patient.
If the instrument is longer than the depth, then it is necessary to place small objects on top of the covering of the womb's depth: so that the entire instrument is prevented from entering into the depth of the womb: and it is necessary to place the spiral, which runs in the instrument, on the upper side: and to hold the instrument, and for the assistant to revolve the spiral until the depth of the womb is opened.
When therefore the abscess appears and is touched by hand and it is soft and tender: then it is necessary to cut it at its head with a broad scalpel.
When therefore the pus is drained, then it is necessary to place on the wound a linen soaked in rose oil: or green oil, which has some astringency: and place the linen, and remove the incision deeply within the womb.
And place externally on the womb and on the sieve clean wool soaked in water, in which crabs have been boiled.
Then it should be treated after two days with an ointment that is suitable for it, until it heals.
And sometimes the womb and the wound are washed by being irrigated with water and honey: then with water in which the root of lily or long aristolochia has been boiled: then return to the ointment.
If the wound is hidden inside the womb, then it is necessary that you refrain from treating it with iron, but rather treat it with what we have said in the division.
Chapter LXXIV.
Instructions for Obstetrics, how to treat live embryos that have been expelled in an unnatural form.
It is necessary for the obstetrician to know first the natural form of childbirth.
From its signs, therefore, it is that when you see a woman compressed in the lower parts, and desires to breathe in air, and finds relief from what is upon her of the childbirth, and the exit of the embryo is hastened: then know that this birth is according to the natural form, and its exit is head first, with the afterbirth with it: or suspended, or hanging from the navel.
When therefore you see these signs, then it is necessary that his belly be compressed, so that the embryo descends quickly.
For when it descends over its head, the afterbirth descends with it, and it is cleansed of those excesses by a good cleansing.
Whoever is born besides this birth is unnatural, unpraiseworthy.
For sometimes the fetus exits feet first, and its body comes out before its head, and one of its feet or hand; or its head and hand come out; or the umbilical cord comes out: and it may turn around its neck, and similar unpraiseworthy configurations.
It is therefore necessary for the obstetrician to be wise and subtle in all these matters, and to beware of error and deception: and I am showing every configuration among them, and how the method is in it, and what it signifies, and to stand by it.
When the fetus exits head first in its natural manner, and it becomes violent for the woman, and the labor becomes difficult for her, and you see that her strength is now weakened: then make her sit on a seat, or let women hold her: and steam her vulva with fenugreek decoction, and with moist oils.
Then the obstetrician should insert a small spatula between her fingers, and use it to tear the afterbirth, and cut it with her nail until the moisture inside flows out: and press the woman's belly until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, then the woman must be given an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesamin oil.
Then instruct her after the enema to be compressed: and make her sneeze with condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour. For the fetus will come out immediately.
If two hands of the fetus come out first, you must gradually and easily bring them back. If it does not obey at the entrance, then place the woman on a seat and lift her feet upwards: then shake the seat on the ground: and the woman should be held so that she does not fall during the shaking.
If therefore the hands do not come out and the fetus dies: then cut them and extract the remainder of the fetus: and tie its hand with a cloth, and extract it equally: for it will come out.
The embryo exits on its feet. When the fetus exits on its feet, then it is necessary to push them upwards: then gradually turn the fetus: afterwards level it.
Then take one of its feet and extend it gradually.
When they come out up to the thighs, then instruct her to be compressed, and make her sneeze with condisi: for it will come out, if God wills.
And if it does not come out with what we have mentioned, then gradually bring the fetus back until you place it according to its natural position. For it will then come out with an easy delivery.
If it is prevented with all that we have mentioned: then take from the mucilage of alum, and oil of sesame, and dissolved gum: and pound everything in a mortar well: then anoint with it the womb of the woman, and below her belly. Then make her sit in warm water until she achieves hypochondria.
When therefore you see that her lower parts are already heated, then give her a sieve of myrrh: and administer it. When therefore she holds the sieve for one hour, then make her sit on a seat. Then make her sneeze: and hold her mouth and nose: and press the lower part of her belly with a gentle pressure. For the fetus will come out immediately.
The exit of the fetus is over the thighs and hands. When it exits in this manner, then she will be able to gradually insert her hands. Then the woman should lie back on her neck, and let her feet hang down below: and she should be lying on the bed, and fold her hands. Then press on her belly gradually. Then remove what is under her feet from the cushions, until she is prepared on the lower part. If the fetus does not come out, then take her feet, and move them with violent motion. Then press what is above the hypochondrium gradually, until the fetus ascends to the upper parts. Then he should insert his hand and gradually adjust the fetus: and instruct the woman to compress herself until the fetus exits.
The exit of the fetus hanging transversely from the hands. Skill will be required in the reduction of his hand. If he cannot reduce it, then lift the woman and make her walk.
If she cannot walk, then make her lie on a bed: and shake her legs with a violent shaking.
Then apply the liniment that you have prepared from mucilages.
If labor begins for her, then make her sit on a seat. Then attend to the reduction of the hand, and align the fetus according to its natural position: and make the woman sneeze, and instruct her to compress herself until it exits.
The exit of the fetus over its neck, with hands spread out, and its face is towards the back of its mother. The midwife must hold the hand of the fetus, then gradually revolve it, and align it with ease.
When it is aligned, then place on its mouth what we have mentioned made from oil and mucilages.
Then instruct her to move gradually. Therefore when you have done that, then make her sit on a seat, and command her to lean to the right side. Then command her to hold it in: and make her sneeze when you apply it.
The exit of the prepared fetus on the side. When it descends to the opening of the matrix in this way with the afterbirth, then tear the afterbirth with your nail until it is emptied of moisture.
If it is suspended over the face of the fetus and its neck, then cut it from the navel: so that it is not retained, and causes death.
Then push the fetus inward until you place it as is proper: and command the woman to bear down several times: for it will come out with a slight effort.
The birth of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins are often born: and sometimes three, and four are born. However, that is unusual, and rarely happens.
Five is beyond nature, and they do not live at all: and one afterbirth contains them, although they multiply, and are separated by a siphon, distinguishing the tied cord of each of them.
And sometimes they exit like a single fetus does in a natural, easy birth: and they exit in an unpraiseworthy manner, as we have mentioned.
If some of them are difficult at birth, and they reach what we have said about unnatural shapes, then treat them as we narrated: and let it be by a subtle midwife, and do what is done with ease and slowness, and adapt according to every shape with what is prepared for it guided by skill leading to health.
Remember what is formed in the womb from embryos and is aborted.
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and more than ten are formed in the womb: and it has already been verified by me that a woman aborted seven, and another fifteen, all fully formed.
That which was done by the measurement of the glorious wise man.
Therefore, all of this must be known by the obstetrician. For perhaps she may encounter something similar to that; therefore, she should oppose it with what is necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
Regarding the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus with what I have said in the division on medication, and it does not come out, and you are forced to use manualoperation with handmanual operation
If therefore the woman is of sound health, and there is not with her any from accidents, from which loss to her is feared: then it is necessary that the woman lie on her back on the bed, and let her head be inclined downwards, and her legs raised: and a servant should hold her on both sides, or she should be tied to the bed, so that her body is not pulled out during the extraction of the fetus.
Then moisten the mouth of the womb with wet oils mixed with alum root, fenugreek, and flaxseed.
Then the midwife should anoint her hand with these oils and mucilages: then she should insert it into the womb with ease. Then she should seek with it the place where the hooks can be fixed to the fetus, and the suitable places for that.
Consider then if the fetus is prepared to descend headfirst: then fix the hooks into its eyes, or on its neck, or in its mouth, or on its palate, or under its chin, or on its clavicle, or in places near the ribs, and under the hypochondria.
If, however, the descent is feet first, then [fix the hooks] on its shins and its middle ribs.
And it is necessary that she hold the hook with her right hand: and place its curvature between the fingers of her left hand: and insert it with ease, and fix the hook in one of those places we mentioned, until she reaches the empty space.
Then fix another hook opposite it, or a third if needed: so that the contraction is equal, and does not lean to one side.
Then it should be extended with equal extension, and the extension should not be according to straightness only, but it should be moved in every direction so that its exit is eased: as is done with a tooth during its extraction.
And it is necessary in that which is between them, so that the extension may be softened. If a part of it is retained, then the midwife must anoint certain fingers with oil and insert them partially to turn with them what is retained.
If therefore a part of the fetus is exiting, then switch the hooks to a higher place: do this until the entire fetus exits.
If therefore the hand exits before other parts and it is not possible to reduce it due to its constriction: then it is necessary that a cloth be wrapped over it. Then extract it until it is completely out, and cut it either at the ankle joint or at the elbow: and you should do this for the other hand and both feet.
If the fetus's head is large, or it encounters constriction upon exit, or there is accumulated water in its head: then it is necessary to insert Spatumile spinosum between the fingers, and split the head with it, and extract the water: or break it with an instrument called Almisdac: whose form comes with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter that follows this one.
Similarly, if the fetus has a large head, then it is necessary to cut with algengematu: or extract it with misdach, as we have said. Then draw out the bones with forceps.
If the head protrudes and is constricted at the fork, then it should be incised until the moisture in the chest is released.
If it is not disentangled and does not obey the exit: then cut off the head piece by piece, as much as you can.
If there is an abscess in the lower part of the abdomen, or if there is dropsy in it: then you must pierce it until the fluid runs out.
If the fetus is on its feet, then its extraction is easy, and its direction towards the maternal opening is simple.
If it is constricted at the belly or chest: then you must extract it with a cloth which you have wrapped over your hand: and incise the belly or chest until what is inside flows out.
If the other limbs are removed and the head returns: then the midwife should insert her left hand. If the maternal opening is open, then insert the hand deeply into the womb and search with it for the head, and draw it with the fingers up to the maternal opening: then insert one hook or two hooks into it, and draw it out with them.
If the maternal opening is constricted due to a warm abscess that has occurred there: then it should not be forced, but instead moist and fatty substances should be applied, and plasters administered: and sit in waters that soften and moisturize.
If the fetus is on its side, then it is possible for it to be aligned: then what we have said about a living fetus should be administered.
If it is not possible to do that, then cut it piece by piece and extract it.
And you must not leave any part of the afterbirth inside at all.
Therefore, when you have completed the operation, then administer what we have said about warm abscesses which occur in the wombs.
If bleeding occurs, then immerse in astringent waters, and administer the rest of the treatment.
And I have indeed seen a woman whose belly contained a dead fetus: then she conceived another on top of it; afterwards, another fetus also died. After a long time, an abscess occurred in her navel, and it swelled until it burst: and it began to discharge pus.
I was called for her treatment, and I treated her for a long time: and the wound did not heal.
I therefore applied to it some strong attracting plasters: and the bone came out from the place. Then after several days, another bone came out. I was therefore amazed by this, since there should not be bone in the belly.
I then thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
I examined the wound and extracted many bones, the woman being in better conditions: and she lived thus for a long time, and discharges a little pus from the place.
And I did not include this foreign element here unless because it contains knowledge and assistance for what the skilled physician administers with hand in the cure.
Chapter LXXVII.
On the forms of necessary instruments for the extraction of the fetus.
The form of the spiral by which the matrix is opened.
Here below is the form of the strictorium, with which the boards are equalized, having two spirals equally at the two ends of two pieces of wood. However, this spiral must be finer than the strictorium: and it should be made either of ebony or buxus wood.
And let the width of the entire piece of wood be almost two fingers: and the edge of each of them is almost one finger, and the length of each is a palm and a half: and in the middle of the two pieces of wood are two additional pieces of the same type of wood, which are already fixed to both, whose length is half a palm and a little more: and the width of each is almost two fingers, or a little more.
And these two additional pieces are inserted into the mouth of the matrix, so that it is opened with them when you turn the two spirals.
Another form similar to that one, finer and lighter.
Let it be made from ebony wood, or boxwood, according to the likeness of forceps. However, at its end there are two additions, as you see here above: and the length of each addition is almost a palm: and the width of each is two fingers.
When you wish to open the matrix with it, then make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging down, with what is between her thighs open. Then insert those two connected additions into the matrix: and you hold the lower end of the instrument between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with scissors, equally according to the amount you wish from the opening of the mouth of the matrix, until the midwife does what she wants.
The form of another vertigo which the ancients called the form of the impeller, by which the fetus is propelled.
The form of Almisdac, by which a large head is crushed: and it resembles forceps, which have teeth at the end, as you see.
And sometimes it is made elongated, like forceps in this form, as you see, which have teeth like a saw's teeth, by which it cuts and crushes.
The form of the hook having one spine.
The form of the hook having two spines.
The form of the spatula having two ends for cutting off the head.
The form of two broad spatulas.
All these instruments are used, and the more their types are multiplied, and they are prepared by the craftsman, the faster they are for their operation, and more esteemed among people because of their quantity.
Therefore, do not disdain any of them so that it may be prepared for you. For the necessity of them is inexcusable.
Chapter LXXVIII.
Regarding the extraction of the afterbirth.
When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, then you must instruct the patient to hold her breath. Then make her sneeze while you press your hand over her mouth and nose. If it exits through this method, it is good.
If not: then take a pot and pierce a hole in its lid. Place herbs that open the matrix os in it, such as reed, rue, dill, chamomile, sage, lignum aloes, and centaury. Take all these herbs or some of them, submerge them in water, and place them over fire.
Then place a tube of reed over the opening of the covered pot, and the other end into the mouth of the matrix: and hold it until the vapor reaches the cavity of the matrix.
Then make her sneeze, as we have said. For the afterbirth will come out easily.
If it remains after this treatment and does not come out: then order the midwife to dip her hand in sesame oil, or coltsfoot mucilage. Then she should insert it into the womb and search for the afterbirth with it. When she finds it, then she should take hold of it and stretch it out gradually.
If it is attached deeply in the womb, then she should insert her hand as we have described until she finds the afterbirth and extracts it gradually straight out, so that the womb does not fall due to a strong pull; rather, it must be moved with ease to the right and left sides; then increase the amount of pulling. For it obeys then, and is preserved, and escapes from adhering.
If the mouth of the womb is constricted, as we have already mentioned: treat it with sneezing and with the medicine from the pot with herbs.
If it does not come out with all that we have mentioned, then be careful not to tire yourself with repeated attempts at extraction.
But it is necessary that which goes out to the mouth of the matrix from it be tied to the woman's hip. Then cleanse her with an ointment of the four-drug mixture. For it will rot her after days, and dissolve, and go out.
However, when it putrefies, a bad smell rises from it to the stomach and head, and harms the weakened area. Therefore, appropriate fumigations should be administered to it.
However, some of the ancients have already experienced fumigations with mustard and dried figs.
The form of the instrument with which a woman is fumigated in the case of retained afterbirth and menses.
Let it be made from a bull's horn similar to aalcama, or from an ox horn: and the wider end should be placed over fire: and the fumigation should be placed on the coals: hold it until that fumigation is consumed: and repeat with another.
Chapter LXXIX.
Regarding the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many children are born with their anus not perforated, which has already been covered by a thin membrane. Therefore, the midwife should pierce it with her sharp finger: and if not, pierce it with an acute spatula: and she should be careful of the muscle, so as not to touch it.
Then place upon it wool soaked in wine and oil. Then care for it with ointments until it heals.
If you fear that it may prolapse, then place a tube of lead in the opening for many days, and remove it when the boy wants to defecate.
And it has also happened that an anal prolapse occurred due to the healing of a wound or an abscess. Therefore, that hardened area should be cut, then it should be treated with what we have said about treatment and lead.
Chapter LXXX.
On the treatment of fistulas which occur in the lower part.
Fistulas which occur in the lower part are nodules and thickening which happen near the anus externally: or in the space of one region: and it is one fistula or multiple fistulas.
When that nodule becomes old, it opens, and a watery white moisture or thin pus runs from it.
And sometimes these fistulas are penetrating. Therefore, penetrating fistulas are recognized by what exits with waste matter and gas when the patient evacuates: and perhaps worms may exit from them.
And among these are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder and to the urethra when they are in that space. And among these are those that penetrate to the hip joint and to the coccyx.
From which it is known that the penetrating fistula goes up to the anus and also from the non-penetrating one is that you insert your index finger into the anus: and insert a thin probe of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
If there is twisting in it, then insert a thin probe made of lead into it, or a hair from horse's mane, until you feel the probe or the hair on your finger.
If you do not feel it thoroughly, and nothing comes out of the hole from excretion, nor wind, nor worm as I said: then you know that it is non-penetrating: therefore hurry to the treatment.
And when the fistula penetrates to the bladder or to the urinary tract: then its indication is the discharge of urine from it, and the prevention thereof so that the area may be healed with medicines.
If it is penetrating to the hip joint or to the hip bone: then the sign of it is that the probe reaches there if there is no twisting up to the bone: and the discovery of pain around the part, and that pus comes out of it always: and that medication does not work in it, nor does it heal with ointment.
And in all these penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all: and the treatment of them is labor and vanity for him, by foolish doctors, on whom it is formed.
In that which is not penetrating and not old, healing is hoped for with the knife: according to what I tell you, and I have already proven: and it is that the patient lies on their back under your hands: and raise their legs up above their hips, and their hips should be inclined towards their abdomen. Then they will insert a lead or tin probe if there is a twist in the fistula until you know where the probe reaches.
If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your index finger into the anus.
If you feel that the probe has already penetrated on its own when inserted, beyond what you feel between your finger and the fistula itself or the flesh: then you will certainly know that it is penetrating. Do not labor over it, for there is no cure for it, as we have said.
They said, however, that the flesh is healed in some men and that there is hope of benefit from the treatment, which is to heat a fine cauterizing instrument according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before, and to insert it heated into the fistula until it reaches near the anus. Then repeat this two or three times until you know that all the additional filtered flesh, which is similar to the tube of a bird's feather, has been burned.
Then treat it with lint wrapped in butter until the burned flesh comes out; then treat it with ointments that generate flesh and consolidate.
If it is healed, that is good.
And if it is not, then it will never be healed with any other treatment.
And if the probe exits and does not reach your finger which is in the anus, and there is a thick veil of flesh or fistula between them, and you see the fistula following the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you go cutting with the probe that is in the fistula until the incision reaches where the end of the probe arrives, and the probe is released and falls out.
Then clean those filtered flesh that resembles a bird's feather tube, so that nothing remains from them.
If blood overcomes you and dissolves the connection between you and your operation so that you cut those flesh: then it is better and quicker to heal by cauterizing it with fire or with sharp medicine.
For cautery with fire brings good properties, the burning of those added flesh, and the cutting off of blood, and the drying of moistures.
Then treat it with linen wrapped in butter, or crushed fat, until the area emits pus, and those burned flesh come out with the pus.
Then treat the wound with consolidating ointments that generate hard flesh: and these medicines have astringent and drying properties.
For when they are restored, then it is already healed: and you do not fear repetition.
If however the fistula has already reached deep into the anus and extends from the excess of the body: then insert your finger into the anus and explore with it.
If therefore you feel resistance, and between you and it there is a veil of sinew or flesh, and it is close to penetration: then there is no operation in that place unless according to the way of confidence and hope.
Which means that one of the three methods is applied to it: either you cauterize it as we said: or you cut it until you reach its hollow, so that it is possible for you to insert linen and treat it closely. And do not proceed much with the cutting so as not to cut the tendon containing the anus, and involuntary discharge may occur in the patient. Then treat it with what we have said.
For it may be healed: or you may extend the membrane itself, and clean it after you cut it up to near the anus, as we have said, using a probe or another instrument with a sharp end. Then clean the filtered flesh that is in the incision as far as you can with probing.
Then attempt the restoration of the entire wound with the incision, and the upper opening where it is healed: and an Fistula remains open on the inner part of the anus, and it will be milder for the patient.
And sometimes the Fistula is sutured in this manner: and it is when you insert a probe into the Fistula: and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with the skin and the edge of the anus: then take a probe with a perforated end, which is like a tanner's needle, that is, of those who prepare hides, in this form. And insert into it a thread wound from five threads, and around it. Then insert the probe with the thread into the Fistula until it reaches its cavity.
If it penetrates near the inner edge of the anus, then pull the thread out from that opening: so that you insert your finger into the anus and pull out the end of the thread, and bring both ends together: and tie them tightly, and leave it for one day or two days: and the more the thread cuts into the flesh, tighten it well until the flesh between the two ends of the thread is cut and falls off: then treat the wound until it heals.
If however the opening of the fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrate by whatever means is prepared for you, unless it is very deep. For it is not within you to do that because of the flap, so as not to cut it.
Then do with it as we have said, until it heals.
The form of the spiked spatula with which the fistula is split, whose curvature is very sharp, and the other part is not sharp, so as not to cut what does not need to be cut, as you see.
Chapter LXXXI.
About the suturing of hemorrhoids, from which blood runs from their incision: and the treatment of fissures.
There are hemorrhoids in two ways. For they are either inside the anus, resembling coal sacs or ember sacs: or they are like grains of a grape. And among them there are small ones and large ones: and blood runs from them always, and there is one, and there are many. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those which are outside the anus are mostly lacking in moisture, from which yellow water or a little blood runs continuously: and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of that which is inside the anus is to instruct the patient to sit: and it should be pressed, until the anus protrudes, and the hemorrhoids become apparent to you. Therefore hang them with hooks: or hold them with your nail. Then cut them at their roots.
If they do not hold the hooks, because of their moisture and softness: then take them with a coarse cloth, or with a mitten made of double wool, and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them, and powder over them after the incision certain warm powders, so that they may serve as a substitute for cauterization. Or cauterize them according to what was precedented in the chapter on cauterizing. Then care for them with the rest of the treatment until they heal.
If the anus does not obey the evacuation, then administer an enema to the patient that contains a slight irritant, so that it washes with what is in the anus, and obeys the evacuation quickly when the patient expels it.
If however the hemorrhoids are external to the anus, then their treatment is light, easy: and it is as you take them with your nail, or take them with a hook, and cut them. Then care for them with what we have said until they heal.
And for those who shrink from incision with iron, then it is necessary to administer their suture in this manner. Take the wrapped thread and insert it into the needle. Then pull the hemorrhoid upward, and make it penetrate with the needle at its root from the other side: and wrap both ends of the thread around the lower part of the needle, and let them be horizontal: and bind the hemorrhoid with a strong ligature. Then knot the thread, and remove the needle.
Do this with all the athelil, and leave one of them untouched: do not sew it up, so that the excess blood may flow out from it.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote over the anus, and put it on the anus: and instruct the patient to rest. Then leave it until it falls off.
When the athelil fall off, care for them with ointments and the rest of the treatment until they heal.
On the Treatment of Fissures. For they often occur from the dryness of the stool and the constriction of the natural functions.
When they become old and medicine does not heal them, then it is necessary to scrape them with the point of a spatula or with your nail until they become moist, and remove the outer layer that prevents them from healing. Then care for them until they heal properly.
If they do not heal, then scrape them more forcefully than before until they bleed heavily, and remove the outer layer; then care for them until they heal.
On the Treatment of Inverted and Non-inverted Almirmar, and Dry Athelil, and Ants.
Chapter LXXXII.
You should know that Almirmar is nothing but a round knot according to the color of the body, similar to the head of a nail: and it occurs throughout the whole body, especially in the lower parts of the feet, and fingers: and pain happens because of them while walking.
Therefore, it must be cut around the nail, and held with scissors, or with a hook, and rooted out from its root.
Then care for it: and if you wish, cauterize it according to what has been precedented in its chapter.
From dry athelil, however, there is a small prominence, rough, filtered, round on the surface of the body. And they often occur in the hands of children.
And the treatment of it is to stretch the athelil, and cut it: or tie it with silk thread: or with hair, until it falls. And if you wish, cauterize it according to what has been mentioned with fire, or with sharp medicine: and now the athelil are rooted out, both inverted and not inverted with the instrument that I shall mention.
Formica is also a small, filtered, thick prominence on the surface of the body, going very deep: and when cold encounters it, it feels like the bite of an ant, and it occurs throughout the whole body: and most of it occurs in the hands.
And the treatment of it is to take a tube from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather: and place that tube over the Formica, until the circle of the tube contains parts of it. Then turn your hand with the cannula until you cut what is around the Ant: and place it deep into the flesh, and root out the Ant from its base.
And if you wish, do it with a cannula of brass or iron, according to this form.
Let the upper part of the cannula be drawn out to a hollow point, so that the grasp upon the finger and its turning may be eased.
And if you wish, cauterize the Ant according to what has been stated about the cauterization of Athelil in the chapter on the cautery.
Chapter LXXXIII.
Concerning the forms of instruments used for enemas in illnesses of the anus, and for relieving the bowels, and colic.
Sometimes an enema is made of silver, or brass, or cast metal, or hammered metal.
And sometimes these instruments are made small and large according to those in which they are used.
Therefore, that which is used in the treatment of small children should be small: and for those whose anuses are weak or painful, so should their enemas be.
Large enema.
Its tube, that is, the upper head where the bag is tied, should be wide according to this manner: and it should have a division so that the bag can be tied as you see, and its lower end which is inserted into the anus should be closed, that is, not open, very soft, drawing towards fineness: and on one side of it there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
And let the width of the hole be according to the thickness of the rays, and a little thicker, and let there be a container in which medicines are placed made from an animal's bladder: or from sheep's parchment, which should be in the form of a small asofrati: whose root is one palm.
And let it be pierced with many holes as it revolves, and let the space that is between each hole be the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those holes strong thread made from raw fiber, which should be of ten strands, or about that number, and attach it to the container like a small asofrati. When the container is placed in it, let it be tied tightly at the head of the enema between two separators with a strong binding. Then administer the enema with it.
And this is the form of the circle and the holes of the container depicted here.
The quality of administering the enema with it is: to fill the container or bladder with medicine that is warmed according to the quantity tolerable by the patient: and beware that it is not too hot or too cold.
Then the patient should lie on their back, and raise their legs upwards: and place under them a cushion, that is, skin upon which people lie, or a linen cloth.
Then anoint the end of the enema with oil, or with sheep's grease, or with fenugreek mucilage, or similar substances. Then insert it into the anus with ease. Then let the assistant take the bladder with both of his hands at once, and squeeze it forcefully until he evacuates everything that is in the clyster into the intestine.
Then remove the clyster, and let the patient raise his legs against the wall.
If the medicine forces it to come out, then hold as much as possible. And if he sleeps with it all night, it is more ultimate in alleviation.
If you give him a clyster for diarrhea and its discharge is rapid: then repeat the clyster until he is healed.
If there are hemorrhoids or painful abscesses in the anus, then let the clyster be very fine and mild, such as those with which children are given clysters.
And this should be the form of a fine clyster for which the skin is tight.
Chapter LXXXIV.
I have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds that befit the book, and I will speak here of their treatment with the hand and with medicines according to completion.
I say, therefore, that wounds vary according to the instrument by which they are inflicted and according to the place on which the wound falls.
The things by which wounds are inflicted are often various, such as being hit by a stone, or cut by a sword or a dagger, or struck with a lance, wood, or an arrow, and similar objects.
Wounds however which are made according to places of the body are, like a wound which falls upon the head, or neck, or chest, or abdomen, or spleen: and similar from those members.
And I am telling the treatments of some wounds, so as to set that reasoning and rule on the other wounds.
And I will begin with simple wounds of the head: for the discussion of compound wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
I therefore say. When a simple wound occurs on the head and there is no fracture of the bone: then consider if it is from the throwing of a stone or similar objects, and it has only broken the skin: and the wound is large, and you fear an unfavorable outcome of a hot abscess: then hurry and immediately bleed the cephalic vein: and do not delay this: and draw out blood according to the strength of the patient: if there is nothing preventing bleeding, especially if little blood comes from the wound. And let the bleeding be from the opposite side of the wounded area.
And let the bleeding be from the opposite side of the wounded area. And let the patient avoid fullness, wine, and heavy foods.
If something prohibits bleeding, then let the diet be reduced, and let the patient avoid meats and wines.
And apply to the wound, if a hot abscess occurs, a cloth soaked in rose oil alone or with wine that has a styptic quality.
If however you are safe from warm abscess, then place on the wound, if it is new with its own blood, and air has not changed it, the powder which I will tell of shortly: and if air has already changed it, then place on it some ointments, until it heals.
If however the wound is large, or is from a sword cut, and similar: and its lips do not come together with small pins, then bring them together with suture, according to what I will tell about sutures in wounds of the belly.
If however the wound is already separated from the bone, and hangs loose, and there is no retention of it except by a small sling: then cut it open. Then treat the wound with medicines, and restore hard flesh instead of skin, and advise the patient to nourish themselves with foods that are thick, such as heads, and cooked wheat until it is like porridge: and things similar to these.
If you find putrefaction in the skin, and it does not adhere to the bone: then cut out all the putrefied part and discard it: then treat it.
If however in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows: and it is not stopped by medicines, then apply something over the artery. If then you find it uncut, then cut it with a lancet, or tie it off. If necessity demands that what we have said does not suffice, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped.
If however these wounds are small, simple, then their matter is easy, light: so that you powder on them this powder: for it consolidates them before air changes them.
Method of the flesh-forming powder. Take one part of frankincense, and two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unburned lime: grind all thoroughly, and sieve it: and fill the wound with it, and bind it tightly, until it adheres well to it, and coagulates with the blood.
Then bind it tightly with bandages, and leave it, and do not loosen it as long as it remains, so that it does not become pus-filled. For the medicine should not be removed until it is healed.
And sometimes the lime alone does this, when you do not have frankincense present, and dragon's blood also performs the same operation on many large wounds, when it is appropriate to place it on them and bind them, and the wounds are fresh with their own blood, which has not been altered by air.
If the air has already altered them in some way, especially when it is during the summer season, then there is no purpose in applying this powder: therefore, treat it with what we have said, so that you place some digesting ointments on them: or place on them poultices made from barley flour, made with water and honey, until they discharge pus. Then treat them with the rest of the treatment until they are healed.
If however a fracture occurs with the wound in the bone, and it is small, then extract it with forceps: and I will now speak of the treatment of head fractures in what is to come.
On wounds of the neck.
If, however, a wound occurs on the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between it and a simple head wound.
If, however, a nerve or artery in the neck is already cut: then if it is a nerve, there is no skill involved except to treat it with substances that have strong astringent properties, such as zinziber and zegi, and similar things. For they harm the nerves and contract them.
And you should not apply anything cold at all to the wound: for the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is higher than other members: and let that with which it is cured be mild from medicines, such as lime washed several times with sweet water and infused with oil, or with rose oil, and turpeth, when it is also washed with sweet water: and other mineral stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
If the wound is large, then apply a suture: or compress its edges with bandages. Then treat it until it heals.
If the wound has depth, or a sinus has formed in its lower part where pus has already collected, then puncture it at the most depressed area.
If the artery has already been cut in the wound and its flow of blood follows: then separate or cut it and tie it up: or cauterize it if the necessity requires this.
If the thyroid cartilage has already been cut through, or entirely, and the vocal cords are saved: then bring together the skin edges with sutures over the thyroid cartilage canal, and do not touch the throat, rather level it, and restore it to its natural shape. Then bind it with a suitable bandage, and leave it for several days. Then treat it with ointments that have astringent and drying properties until it heals.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then examine it: if there are fragments of bone in it, remove them all, or as many as you can: and what does not prepare, leave it until the wound putrefies, and it separates and its discharge is alleviated.
If the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on it the powder I have mentioned. If bone appears in the wound and forms a fistula: then treat it with what is mentioned in its own chapter.
Regarding the wound in the spatulas.
If there is a puncture from a lance or a knife: and you see its depth, then examine it. If wind or gas escapes from the wound when the patient breathes on it, then you know that the wound is mortal.
If it does not have depth and is fresh with its blood: then do not apply powder to it from the first hour, nor bind it, so that blood is not retained in its depth, and returns to the heart, and kills the patient: but apply a drawing ointment to it, and dissolve it twice a day.
If ointment is not available to you, then apply an old cottar on the wound opening, so that it draws out what comes from its moisture: and make the patient sleep over the wound, so that what gathers in it flows out.
If three days have passed for the wound, or more, and spasms have not occurred to the patient, nor bad palpitations of the heart, nor constriction in breathing, and you see his other conditions good: then know that the wound is healing. Treat it with lint and other treatments until it is healed.
If its healing is hindered and it is now always open, then know that it has become a fistula. Treat it according to its chapter.
And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple on the surface of the chest or back: then treat it with what precedes from stitching, if it is large: or with powder, if it is small.
If it has already made an impression on the bone and fragments have broken off: then examine the wound and quickly remove those fragments if they are separate. If they are not separated, then leave them until the wound becomes putrid, for their extraction is eased.
The judgment in the treatment of other wounds occurring in the other parts is the same as what we have said.
About wounds of the abdomen, and the protrusion of the intestines, and their treatment.
The disruption that occurs in the abdomen is major, medium, and minor.
From a major disruption, the intestine or a number of intestines sometimes protrude.
Therefore, their insertion and suture is more forceful and difficult.
And a minor disruption also becomes difficult in another way. It follows, therefore, that their reduction is more difficult if you do not promptly return them to their place immediately: because it swells, opens, and enlarges; hence its entry becomes difficult.
Therefore, the medium disruption is better: because with it, the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is difficult in these two types.
Know that the suture of the abdomen is according to four methods.
Two common sutures are used for the suture of the abdomen and the suture of other wounds of the body: and two other sutures are specifically used for the other wounds. However, they are more suitable for stitching the abdomen: and I tell you each one with explanation, and description.
I say therefore, that when a wound is small, and something of the intestine protrudes from it, and it becomes difficult to reduce it: then this is due to one of two methods. Either because of the smallness of the tear, as we have said: or because there is inflation in the intestine due to the cold air.
Therefore, when it is thus, then you must warm it, so that you submerge a sponge or a wet cloth in warm water alone. Or boil squash, cyperus, and spike with it, and apply it to the intestine until the inflation resolves.
Sometimes it does this with wine that has astringent properties: and it is better than water alone for resolving the inflammation.
Therefore, when you see the inflation resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which althea or mallows have been boiled. For by this its entrance is softened with a small thing.
If however its return occurs after this treatment, then find and slightly cut into the tear with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids.
And the first treatment is better when prepared than surgery: and there should be no coercion to cut after necessity and lack of instruments.
Let one part of it be curved, sharp, and the other part not sharp, and the tip should be fine but not as fine as a spatula, rather slightly blunted: and it is that which resembles a calamus, as you see.
When therefore the wound enlarges and enters the intestine, then it is necessary that it be reduced to its natural form in its proper place if possible; for it is better.
When however the tear is wide in the lower part of the belly: then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and place his legs higher than his head. And if it is in the upper part of the belly, then place his head and chest higher than his lower parts.
And similarly if there is a tear in one of the two parts of the belly, then direct your attention and your consideration always to this, that the part which has the wound be higher than the other part.
And thus it is necessary to administer it in great wounds and in medium wounds.
In small wounds, place it according to how it is prepared for you.
Then make sure that a devout assistant is present at your side, who holds the entire tear with his hand: and bring together its lips. Then reveal to him who follows the suture bit by bit: and this is the method of a common suture.
And it is to take a needle, or a number of needles according to the quantity of the wound's width. Then leave the width of one finger, that is, the physician's ring finger, from the end of the tear: and insert one needle with thread at both ends of the skin, passing through to the underlying tissue with both ends until it penetrates from the other side, and you have now brought together two ends of the skin and two ends of the underlying tissue: and there are four layers.
Then tie with double thread around the wound several times from both sides simultaneously until the two lips of the wound are joined by a proper union.
Then measure the thickness of the finger as well, and insert another needle; then tie it with thread, as you did with the first needle. Therefore, do not stop doing this with the needles you need until you complete the constriction of the entire wound.
And the needles should be of medium thickness between thick and thin: because very thin needles quickly penetrate the flesh: and thick ones have difficult entry into the skin: for this reason they should be of medium thinness and thickness.
And it should not be that the needle is inserted at both ends of the nearby skin: so that the flesh is not cut quickly, and the wound is opened before its consolidation, and they are not stretched even with the suture: so that the wound is not prevented from consolidating.
Then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not harm the patient during their sleep: and place small pieces of cloth from clothes on all sides to hold the ends of the needles: and leave them until you know that the wound is already consolidated.
And this type of stitching with needles is particularly suitable for small wounds. Because one needle, or two, or about that number is sufficient for stitching them.
The second common stitching method is to join the four ends with stitching: the two ends of the skin and the two sinew ends together at once, using a needle on which thread equally thin and thick is wound.
Then when you have penetrated with the needle these four ends, withdraw the needle from the side where you started in the same way, so that the woven thread falls from the upper part of the wound: so that it is a suture, just like the suture of cloth by which cloths are joined, and place between every suture the thickness of a little finger.
But men know this suture.
And with this suture I sewed the wound that had occurred to a man in his abdomen, who had been wounded with a dagger, and the tear of the wound was more than one palm: and about two palms had protruded from the middle intestine, and there was a rupture in the middle of the abdomen.
I therefore replaced it after his intestine had been outside the wound for twenty-four hours.
The wound healed in about fifteen days: and I cared for him, and he was healed: and he lived many years after that, in his usual condition.
And the doctors had judged that he would not be healed.
And it was miraculous that I did not cure it with an ointment. For I was in a place where no ointment could be found, nor any other medicine. I therefore placed an old poultice on the wound twice a day, and continually washed it with honey water until it was healed.
I will now describe two types of sutures according to the account of the discourse.
And it is that you begin with a sharp suture: and insert the needle from the outer to the inner part.
When therefore the needle penetrates the skin, and goes into the flesh according to the length and breadth of the whole body: leave the end that you inserted the needle on one side, and make it penetrate to the other end from the inner part to the outer part at the other end.
When therefore you make it penetrate, then make it penetrate according to this at the same end of the flesh from the outer part to the inner: and leave the end that is on this side, and make the needle penetrate to the other end from the inner part to the outer part: and make it penetrate with your penetration as you make it penetrate in the end of the flesh which is in its part, until it penetrates the whole of it.
Then begin again from this same side, and sew it with the end that is from the other side, and draw the needle out from the skin which it penetrated.
Then return it to that skin, and sew the end of the flesh that is on the other side with this end of the wound: and draw it out from the skin which is on its part, and do this alternately, one after another: and do this turn by turn until you sew the whole externally according to this example.
And the essence of this suturing is to sew the sutures of the skin as they are skins: so that you sew the flesh alternately from one side of the end of the skin: and leave it alternately from the other side until you complete it.
The second kind of proper suture, which Galen said.
His speech was narrated to describe it according to the similarity by which some of the physicians do it, so that they bring together each part to its corresponding comparable part naturally: and they apply the end of the lip to its other end, and the end of the eyelid to its other end. And it is done according to what I narrate to you.
You must fix the needle in the end of the eyelid near you from the outer side, and make it penetrate to the inner side in that place only: and leave the two ends of the lip. Then turn the needle, and make it penetrate from the outer side to the inner side at both ends of the lip, on both sides.
Then turn both, make both penetrate from the inner to the outer side at both ends of the eyelid, which are on the opposite side.
And this method of suturing is better than the common easy suture, and it is the suture of which the previous mention was made.
This is therefore the teaching of Galen as well.
And some said. The abdominal suture is corrected with two needles. This is to insert one thread into both of them: and begin with the insertion of the needle, from the side that is nearer to you, and make it penetrate all the way to the other side, according to the suture of those who have equal skin.
And you shall know that when there is a rupture in the middle of the abdomen: then its suture is more difficult than that of the other parts of the abdomen.
The judgment of the treatment of a wound is the judgment of the other wounds.
This is because when you encounter a fresh wound with its blood before the air alters it: and you reduce the intestine, and restore it to its place, and adjust it: then apply powdered meat-jelly on it.
If the air has already altered the wound: then apply some ointments that are available to you until they produce pus: and let the threads fall out, and let the wound consolidate and heal. Then treat it as is the treatment of other wounds, until it heals.
If the medicines are not available to you, then apply old dung on it immediately when it starts to emit pus: and change it twice a day, as I have taught you, until it heals.
For you do not need other treatments in most cases when wounds are simple.
If you fear that the wound communicates with the principal members in the injury, then it is necessary to soak a soft wool in oil of moderate heat, or in rose oil: and place it around the areas between the groin, and under the armpits.
If he feels pain, or pricking, or putrefaction in his intestines (for this often happens), then administer an enema with astringent, black, warm wine: especially if the putrefaction has already reached the intestine and has caused a discharge penetrating to its concavity.
And you know that which is from the large intestine is of easier healing; and that which is from the small intestine is of harder healing.
And the intestine which is called the jejunum does not admit healing from a wound that occurs in it at all: and this is because of the multitude of its veins, and their largeness, and because of the fineness of its body, and its closeness to the nature of nerves.
If what protrudes from the wound is cicatricial tissue, and you encounter it fresh: reduce it according to your method of reduction, by which you equally reduce intestines.
If however time has passed, and it has already become green or black: then it is necessary to tie it with a thread above the place which has turned black, so that blood flow does not occur. For in cicatricial tissue there are veins and arteries.
Then cut what is beyond that ligature, and place the two ends of the thread hanging from the lower part of the wound outside it: so that the pulling on it is eased for you, and its extraction in the case of cicatricial tissue, and the discharge of pus from the wound.
 Recall of the wound that occurs in the intestine.
When a rupture occurs in the intestine, and it is small: then it is possible for it to be restored in some people: therefore, because I have seen someone who was wounded in his abdomen with a lance thrust, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and the wound was old: and a fistula had formed, and excretions and flatulence were discharged from it.
I provided therefore treatment until I was not confident in his healing: nor did I cease to refine it until he was healed, and the place was strengthened.
After I saw the place already strengthened, I was afraid for the patient, that a bad accident might occur in his stomach: and that bad accident did not happen to him. And he remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking, and having intercourse, and entered the bath, and exercised in his diets.
And some of the experienced have already said that when a wound occurs in the intestine and it is small, then it should be tied according to this method. And it is that you take ants with large heads. Then bring together the two lips of the wound, and place one of the ants that have an open mouth on the two lips of the wound. When it bites on them and closes its mouth, cut off its head, for it adheres and does not loosen.
Then place another ant near the first one, and do not cease to do this with each ant after the other according to the extent of the entire wound.
Then reduce it, and sew the wound. For those heads remain attached to the intestine until it is fed and healed, and no harm befalls the patient thoroughly.
And it is now possible to suture the intestine even with a fine thread: which is taken from the intestine of an animal, attached to the needle after it is inserted.
And you take the end of this thread from the gut, and it is cleaned thoroughly. Then tie a fine linen thread wound around its end. Then insert the thread into the needle, and sew with it the gut. Then replace it in the incision.
And this method of sewing with ants and gut is only according to the way of trust and hope.
Know, a wound that is large, wide, especially if it is in one of the thin intestines: then there is no remedy except for narrowing, and there is no healing of it at all.
Regarding the treatment of hemorrhoids and fistulas.
Know, that any wound or abscess when it becomes old and aged, and turns into an ulcer, and does not heal, and constantly emits pus, and does not stop: then it is generally called a fistula wherever it may be on the body, and we call it Zuchemen.
And a fistula indeed is according to truth a hardened, filtered knot, white, with which there is no pain, and it has the concavity of a bird's feather: and because of this some call it Risati, that is, a feather.
And in certain hours, it is moist, emitting pus. And perhaps the moisture splits in certain hours. And sometimes this moisture is much, and is little: and it is thick, and it is thin.
And I have already premised in the division, then when I said wounds, that any ulcer which does not heal, nor flesh is born in it, is not such except for one of nine causes.
One of which is either due to the scarcity of blood in the body: or due to its malignancy: or because there is hard flesh between it and its lips, preventing the birth of flesh: or because it is full of dirt and filth: or because the ulcer itself is putrid, and the matter discharged from it is of bad quality: or because the medicine used for its cure is inappropriate: or because corruption falling in the region is a kind of pestilence, or by the nature of the region, as happens in Caesaraugusta: where the digestion of diseases is difficult, and the healing of abscesses is delayed naturally: or because there is one bone or a number of bones in it.
And I have already shown all these causes and their signs, and their treatments with medicines in the division: and it is necessary here that I make you know the treatment of Fistulas and Zukens, which is done by the method of operation with the hand.
Know therefore that a Fistula occurs in all parts of the body. For among them are Fistulas that reach the large veins and arteries, or nerves, or skin: or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs: or to any of the vertebrae of the spine, or to any of the composite joints: such as the hand and foot: and among them are those that go to the proximity of the main member and similar ones.
Which therefore of these Fistulas is according to this method, is among illnesses difficult to heal, and does not receive treatment, and occupation with it is labor and ignorance.
If there is any fistula whose depth does not reach the places I mentioned: and you hope, and trust in its treatment, and wish to understand it, then take a probe of metal or iron, if the fistula extends straight, and explore it with it.
If there is a twist in the fistula, then investigate it with a fine lead probe. Because lead, with the softness of its body, is lightened and curved around the twist.
If the fistula has many openings, it is not possible for you to indicate on it with a probe. Clysterize therefore one of its openings from its openings.
For the moisture with which you clysterize it goes towards the other openings and runs out from them.
Then carefully inquire according to the way it is possible for you: to know whether there is an opening or nerve, and whether the fistula's depth is far or near: or whether there is one fistula with many openings, and stand over all of this, with your utmost strength: with your questioning of the patient, and by finding pain upon pressing with your hand on the area, and similar signs and causes leading to abscess formation.
Therefore, when you stand on all those true stations, then proceed to the treatment with confidence: and it is that you consider then if the fistula is near and apparent, or in a safe place far from the joint, or from the nerve, or artery, or vein, or one of the places I have mentioned to you: then cut the fistula according to what has been previously stated in my narration, and remove what is in it from the filtration, and corrupted flesh, which is born at its opening from the flesh, or sinew, and similar things: and treat it until it heals.
If however the fistula is of deep length, and it is straight: then it is necessary to cut it deeply as much as possible for you. Then clean it from all its corrupted flesh.
Then apply linen wrapped in sharp medicines: and insert it until the depth of the fistula that you grasped with the iron: do this several times with it until the sharp medicine corrodes all that remains in the depth of the fistula from corruption.
Then treat it with ointments that generate healthy flesh until it is healed.
If however it does not heal by that method, then cauterize it as we have described.
If therefore the cause of the fistula is a bone, and it is confirmed to you: then seek it out, and cut it as I have told you: unless something prevents you from doing so because of a vein, or nerve, or a principal member, as we have said.
If therefore the bone is revealed to you, and there is something of corruption and blackness in it: then scrape it until all of its corruption is removed. Then treat it with what causes flesh to grow on it until it is healed.
If it does not heal, and discharges pus as it did before: then you know that you have not reached the complete eradication of the corruption.
Reveal it again, and thoroughly examine it, and clean it with your utmost strength.
Then restore it. If it is healed, that is good: and if not, then you know that that corruption is in the distant depth of the body, which you have not reached. Therefore, there is no skill for you in it, except to leave it to nature.
If a small bone is corrupted and it is possible for you, pull it out with fine tweezers that are suitable for it.
If there are many bones, then carefully pull out all of them, and do not leave any of them with your strength.
If something from the humors opposes you, and there is no fear or mistake in cutting them: then cut those humors and flesh, if they are there, and free the bones.
If you do not have the preparation for removing bones at your time, then apply something to the wound that will cause it to rot: and leave it until what is around those bones rots from flesh and humors.
And guard the wound so that it does not heal over. And let the incision you made in your operation be constricted. Rather, apply to it, if you fear, some tow soaked in ground sulfur with oil: or tow soaked in Egyptian ointment, or some green ointment.
For when those humors rot and the bones separate from them, the removal of them is eased, and their extraction is alleviated.
If however it is one large bone, like the bone of the leg, or the bone of the hip, and similar to those, and what is corrupted in it is a large part: then scrape it thoroughly until that blackening and corruption are removed. Then restore the wound.
If however what is corrupted in it is a large part, and the corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to saw through it, and cut it entirely up to the place where the corruption reaches: then treat it until it consolidates.
And I tell you of a case that happened to a man in his leg: that you may set it as an example and aid for your operation.
There was a man of about thirty years of age, to whom pain occurred in his leg, caused by something that moved within his body, that is, from the interior, until the matter reached the leg and swelled with a large abscess: and he did not have an external cause.
Therefore, time was wasted with the errors of the physicians until the abscess was opened, and a great deal of matter came out with it. And his treatment was delayed until the leg became fistulated, and many openings were formed in it: all of which discharged pus and bodily fluids.
Therefore, he was treated by a multitude of physicians for about two years, and there was no skilled practitioner until I was called, and I saw his leg and the matter flowing from those openings in great abundance: moreover, the whole body of the man had already wasted away, and his color was yellow.
I therefore inserted a probe into one of the openings, and the probe reached the mouth.
